Important News

Eleventh National Affairs Meeting of the Executive Yuan 63

Today (the 3rd) the Executive Yuan held its eleventh National Affairs Meeting. Those present were Chiang Kai-shek, Sun Fo, Ma Fuxiang, Liu Shangqing, Liu Ruiheng, Wang Boqun, and Kong Xiangxi. Those attending by invitation were Li Jinlun, Chen Shaokuan, Li Shuhua, and Chen Yi. The secretary was Bi Chou, and the director of political affairs was Chen Rong. The meeting was chaired by Chiang Kai-shek. The matters discussed were as follows: (1) A proposal from the Ministry of Education regarding the drafting of measures to guarantee the independence of educational funding, stipulating that all special education funds allocated from national taxes or surcharges, such as likin and surcharges on salt, tobacco, and alcohol taxes, should be allocated by the local national tax authorities according to the original actual amount until reliable compensatory measures are determined, in order to avoid the cessation of education. The question of whether this should be approved for compliance was resolved with an order to the Ministry of Finance to proceed accordingly. (2) The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission submitted proposed revisions to the organizational law of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, requesting approval for referral to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. The resolution was to forward it to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. (3) A resolution was made to reorganize the Opium Prohibition Committee, appointing Liu Ruiheng, Zhang Xueliang, Li Jihong, Zhong Ketuo, Luo Yunyan, Wu Liande, Zhang Shusheng, Tian Xiongfei, Chen Shaokuan, Hu Yuwei, Chen Bingguang, Shi Zanming, and Ma Yinchu as members. Zhong Ketuo was also appointed as the director of the Investigation and Verification Office, and Hu Yuwei as the director of the General Affairs Office. (4) A resolution was made to approve the resignation request of Li Yuying, the president of National Peking University, and to appoint Shen Yinmo as the president of National Peking University. Also, the resignation request of Yi Peiji, the president of National Peking Normal University, was approved, and Xu Bingxu was appointed as the president of National Peking Normal University. (5) A resolution was made to remove Huang Changgu from his substantive post as a member of the Hubei Provincial Government, and Chen Guangzu was appointed to fill the vacancy. (6) A resolution was made to assign Chen Yanjiong, the director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Railways, to another position, and Liang Hancao, a counselor, was transferred to fill the vacancy. The vacated counselor position was filled by Sun Hegao. (7) A resolution was made to assign Han Haicheng, the director of the First Clothing Factory of the Ministry of Military Affairs; Zhou Liang, the director of the First Woolen Mill; and Lu Dengying, the chief of the Clothing Section of the Storage Department of the Military Supplies Bureau, to other positions. Yan Ling, the chief of the Materials Section, requested resignation, which was granted. The vacated position of director of the First Clothing Factory was filled by Lu Dengying, transferred from the position of chief of the Clothing Section of the Storage Department of the Military Supplies Bureau. The vacated position of chief of the Clothing Section was filled by Wang Fengnan. Zhang Naiheng was appointed to fill the vacated position of director of the First Woolen Mill. Liu Shouyu, Zhuang Quan, and Zhang Liangqing were appointed as members of the Ordnance Research Committee of the Ministry of Military Affairs. (8) A resolution was made to transfer Wang Zhangyou to serve as the Salt Transport Commissioner of Lianghuai and Zhang Jun to serve as the Salt Transport Commissioner of Shandong. (9) A request from the Ministry of Finance to appoint Hu Xingchi as the Deputy Salt Transport Commissioner of Huainan was resolved with approval to forward the request for appointment. (10) A request from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to appoint Li Guan and 32 others as secretaries and attachés to various embassies, consuls-general, consuls, vice-consuls, and probationary consuls at various consulates, and a request to remove Liang Yunli and 15 others from their positions as secretaries and attachés to various embassies, consuls-general, consuls, vice-consuls, and probationary consuls at various consulates, was resolved with approval to forward the request for appointment and removal. (11) A submission from the Shandong Provincial Government stating that You Lucheng and Yan Zhenzi, secretaries of the Department of Construction; Kong Lingcan and Zhang Hanying, section chiefs; and Yu Haomin and Xia Yan, technical experts, had resigned one after another, and proposing the appointment of Li Guangzu, Zhang Yuexun, and Shi Jiefan as secretaries of the Department of Construction, Cao Liqing and Hou Guanglu as section chiefs of the Department of Construction, and Zhong Boren, Yu Wuheng, Shi Andong, Zhou Li, and Shen Zongyi as technical experts of the Department of Construction, was resolved with approval to forward the submission for appointment and removal. (12) A submission from the Henan Provincial Government stating that Zhang Sikan and Cheng Zhen, secretaries of the Secretariat; and Feng Baiping, Gao Zhenying, Ding Kangbao, and Luo Tingxian, section chiefs, had left their positions, and Wang Yuan, a secretary, was vacant due to illness, requesting their removal, and proposing the appointment of Xu Wenjing, Cui Weiwo, and He Xuehai as secretaries, and Tong Xikun, Wang Zhenyu, Dong Zhaolin, and Lin Shouren as section chiefs, was resolved with approval to forward the submission for appointment and removal. (13) A request from the Hubei Provincial Government to appoint Chen Bingqian as a technical expert in the Department of Construction was resolved with approval to forward the request for appointment. (14) A submission from the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission regarding the approval of the request from Gongsang Norbu, the League Chief of the Josutu League and concurrently Military Commander Jasagh, to resign from his concurrent position as the Jasagh of the Right Banner of Kharchin, with Dutuobo succeeding to the vacancy, was resolved with approval to forward the submission for appointment and removal.

### The Wuxi Chamber of Commerce Requests Correction of the Business Tax Rate in Jiangsu Province 64

In order to compensate for the loss after the abolition of likin, the Jiangsu Provincial Government has established a business tax, with the Department of Finance drafting regulations for the collection of business tax and detailed implementation rules, which have been approved by the provincial government meeting and will soon be implemented. The Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce believes that the tax rates set by Jiangsu Province, which are almost all between five per thousand and twenty per thousand, are significantly different from the general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces set by the National Likin Abolition Conference in 1928. Therefore, it has specifically raised three points of opinion and telegraphed them to the Ministries of Finance and Industry today, requesting correction, and requesting that the Jiangsu Department of Finance be ordered to postpone the collection temporarily before receiving approval from the ministries. Simultaneously, telegrams were sent to the chambers of commerce in Zhenjiang, Nanjing, and Shanghai, as well as other places, requesting unified advocacy. The telegram to the Ministry of Finance is recorded below:

"We humbly acknowledge that your esteemed ministry replied to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's telegram, stating that the report that Jiangsu Province's planned business tax rates had been increased tenfold from the original guidelines was a false rumor. Merchants and citizens were relieved and rejoiced. However, unexpectedly, news reports indicate that the Jiangsu Provincial Government's 367th meeting passed the business tax regulations and detailed implementation rules, as well as the tax rate schedule, with tax rates mostly between five per thousand and twenty per thousand. What your esteemed ministry suspected to be a false rumor has become a reality in Jiangsu Province, which is deeply alarming. After careful examination of the general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces set by the National Likin Abolition Conference in July 1928, the business tax rates stipulated that the sales industry, manufacturing industry, printing industry, hotel industry, inn industry, entertainment venue industry, and photography industry should be taxed at one to two per thousand of their sales amount. The brokerage industry should be taxed at two per thousand of the brokerage fee. The contracting industry should be taxed at five ten-thousandths of the contract amount. The leasing industry should be taxed at one per thousand of the rental amount. The transportation industry should be taxed at one per thousand of the transportation amount. The money shop industry, pawnshop industry, and warehouse industry should be taxed at one per thousand of the capital amount. The general tax rate was one per thousand, and the highest was no more than two per thousand. The lowest, such as the contracting industry, was only five ten-thousandths. At that time, the Likin Abolition Conference accommodated the opinions of the business community, and the rates were carefully considered and determined. Although provinces could formulate their own flexible measures and tax standards in special circumstances, the tax rates levied should not be higher than the provisions of this general guideline. The intention was extremely prudent. Since the business tax is levied based on business income, regardless of profit or loss, the tax rate can only be expressed as a per thousand ratio and cannot be expressed as a percentage. However, if the per thousand ratio reaches ten, it is no different from a percentage. However, the Jiangsu tax rate schedule lists ninety industries, and the tax rates of fifty-seven industries exceed two per thousand, and forty-eight industries even reach ten per thousand or more. This not only deviates greatly from the general guidelines for business tax set by the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928, but also differs significantly from the fourth article of the general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces recently submitted by your esteemed ministry to the Executive Yuan for promulgation, which stipulates that the business tax rate should be calculated using the per thousand method according to the tax base, and should not exceed two per thousand at most. This is the first point that your esteemed ministry should pay attention to and remedy. As for luxury and other businesses that should be banned, according to the fifth article of the business tax guidelines recently submitted by your esteemed ministry to the Executive Yuan for promulgation, provinces must establish a business tax review committee to collect business tax. It seems that the committee should be established before or with reference to the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928, representatives from chambers of commerce should be convened to participate in the evaluation. Currently, officials are not allowed to concurrently operate businesses. They may not fully understand the situation in the business community, and it is not advisable to interpret things literally, which may cause obstacles. This is the second point that your esteemed ministry should pay attention to and remedy. According to the first article, second item, of the business tax guidelines approved by the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928, business licenses should be renewed annually. The third article of the supplementary measures recently promulgated by your esteemed ministry also stipulates that businesses must apply for a business license within one month after the promulgation of the guidelines and supplementary measures, and in the last month of each subsequent year. The competent authority should determine the annual business tax rate, level, and amount when issuing the business license, and it should not be reduced or increased within that year. The collection period may be determined by each province according to the situation, monthly or quarterly, but the amount of tax should still be calculated annually according to the prescribed tax rate without any ambiguity, to prevent provinces from gradually re-levying taxes monthly or quarterly. This is the third point that your esteemed ministry should pay attention to and remedy. Furthermore, there is something that cannot be left unsaid: Since the government issued a clear order to abolish likin, merchants dare not be overly humble and forget the meaning of 'taking from the people for the people,' nor dare they falsely rely on organizations or engage in other hidden agendas. However, practically speaking, the increased customs duties have already been implemented, and the recently revised tariff has also been appropriately increased. According to the old Treaty of Renyin, the abolition of likin should be able to compensate. However, the original commodity likin has now been mostly converted into consumption tax, and the tax rate may be higher than before. The inconvenience of investigation and searching door-to-door has caused commercial unrest, which is worse than setting up checkpoints everywhere. The merchants' suffering has not been alleviated. The business tax that the provinces are now considering is a new burden for the merchants, who need to develop a habit of paying it. It is a new income for the government, which should pay attention to the source of tax. If the tax rate is too high, not only will the merchants be unable to bear it, but since January of this year, all prices have risen sharply, and the social situation is precarious. A slight increase in the burden will only affect the merchants, but the high prices will affect the entire society. This is what we are worried about. Our association cherishes the idea of sharing the joys and sorrows of the country and dares not suppress this information. Therefore, we urgently submit this report, hoping that you will carefully consider the intention of abolishing likin to save the people and quickly correct the Jiangsu Provincial Government's reported business tax regulations, detailed implementation rules, and tax rate schedule according to the general guidelines for business tax set by the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928, and order Jiangsu Province to temporarily postpone the collection before receiving approval from the ministry, in order to save the merchants from dire straits and ensure social stability. We await your orders with eager anticipation. Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce bows respectfully, Jiang. (The telegram to the Ministry of Industry is omitted as it is the same.)"

Today, the Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce also sent telegrams to the chambers of commerce in Nanjing and Shanghai, as well as the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce, requesting them to telegraph the Ministry of Finance to inquire about the discrepancies between the current general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces promulgated by the ministry and the nine articles of the general guidelines resolved by the Likin Abolition Conference in July 1928, and to request an explanation. The telegram reads as follows: "Jiang sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, and a separate letter will be sent. It has been found that the general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces recently promulgated by the Ministry of Finance and the general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces set by the National Likin Abolition Conference in July 1928, although both have nine articles, differ significantly in content. The most important difference is in the business tax rate. The general guidelines set by the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928 fully stipulated the types and levels in the second article, and they have already been determined separately. However, the recently promulgated guidelines by the ministry divide them into three articles, the second, third, and fourth. The second article stipulates that the types and levels should be determined separately by each province according to the local commercial situation. The fourth article adds a proviso that this does not apply to luxury businesses and other businesses that should be banned. Strictly speaking, businesses that should be banned should not be allowed by the state in the first place. What business tax is there to speak of? Furthermore, the eighth article of the supplementary measures stipulates that the tax base can be up to twenty per thousand of the capital amount. Business tax cannot be expressed as a percentage. Jiang has stated in detail in the telegram to the Ministry of Finance that if the per thousand ratio reaches ten, it is no different from a percentage, let alone exceeding it. How can merchants bear this? Furthermore, the industries that should be exempt from business tax were defined as the fourth article in the general guidelines set by the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928, which included four items: 1. Those with capital less than 500 yuan; 2. Those with annual business income less than 1,000 yuan; 3. Those without shops or signs; and 4. Firewood industry. However, the recently promulgated guidelines by the ministry only list one item in the second article of the supplementary measures, that is, those with capital less than 500 yuan. The rest have been deleted, resulting in the Jiangsu Department of Finance mistakenly listing the firewood industry in the same category as coal and collecting business tax, which is even more harsh. However, according to the Shanghai News on January 21, the Ministry of Finance sent a telegram to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, distributing the general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces, also stating that the general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces resolved by the Ministry of Finance at the National Likin Abolition Committee meeting in July 1928, now that likin and all similar taxes have been abolished, the business tax in various places must be implemented in accordance with the original plan of the Likin Abolition Conference, and the ministry has prepared thirteen supplementary measures, and copied the general guidelines for business tax in various provinces, and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for instructions. It is said that the general guidelines for the collection of business tax in various provinces recently promulgated by the Ministry of Finance were indeed handled in accordance with the original plan of the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928, but why are there differences in the content and articles, and the different articles are all important. According to the fifth article of the recently promulgated guidelines by the ministry, each province should establish a business tax review committee to collect business tax, and its members should include representatives from the chamber of commerce, which shows that the central government does have the intention of sincerely adopting opinions. The general guidelines set by the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928 were determined after careful consideration and are the result of merchants' opinions. As the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce stated in its telegram to the Ministry of Finance on the day, the two taxes currently being discussed, the special consumption tax and the business tax, both have guidelines set at the Likin Abolition Conference, and they must be implemented in accordance with them to avoid abuses. Your esteemed association leads the merchants, and we in the lower regions admire you. We request that you present an explanation to the ministry as to why the recently promulgated business tax guidelines are inconsistent with those agreed upon at the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928, and request that they be implemented in accordance with them to stabilize business and avoid abuses. Therefore, we enclose the general guidelines for business tax set by the Likin Abolition Conference in 1928 as a substitute for a telegram. We await your decision with eager anticipation."

### The Ministry of Finance Abolishes and Merges Huai-Zhe Salt Fields 65

The Ministry of Finance is reorganizing the salt fields, raising the status and authority of the field directors to increase administrative efficiency and merging the field areas to reduce expenses. The original eleven fields in Huainan have been merged into six fields: Miaowan merged with Xinxing, Donghe merged with Anliang, Dingxi merged with Caoyan, Pinjiao merged with Fengjue, Lvsi merged with Yuzhong. The general field director of Tongtai belonged to a transfer agency, which was abolished at the end of December last year. The original twenty-six fields in Liangzhe have been merged into sixteen fields: Xucun merged with Huangwan, Haisha merged with Baolang, Dongjiang merged with Sanjiang, Dasong Chuanzhang merged with Qingquan, Shangwang merged with Shuangsui, Minghe field was abolished, Songjiang's four fields were merged into one field, which is Qingcun and Liangpu merging into Yuanpu, and Chongming field was abolished. All of these changes have been in effect since February 1st. It is said that the standard for the abolishment and merger is based on the overall planning of production, affairs, and transportation.

### Reasons for Liu Shufan's Exclusive Appointment to Postal Savings 66

The Ministry of Communications presented a request to the Executive Yuan to transfer Liu Shufan to be the full-time Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, in recognition of his achievements in handling postal savings and remittance matters, in order to delegate responsibility to him. Long Dafu, the section chief, was promoted to the position of Director of the Postal Department that Liu Shufan originally held concurrently, and Qian Chunqi was appointed to the position of Director-General of the Postal Bureau that Liu Shufan originally held concurrently. All were appointed by the National Government and sworn into office at the auditorium of the Ministry of Communications on February 2nd. The original submission from the Ministry of Communications is recorded below: "Liu Shufan, Director of the Postal Department and concurrently Director-General of the Postal Bureau of this ministry, was specially appointed as the plenipotentiary representative of the Republic of China to attend the Universal Postal Union Congress two years ago. After the meeting, the ministry sent him to Europe, America, and Japan to study postal matters. Afterwards, he reported that the postal savings and remittance business in various countries was extremely successful, and that our country should emulate it. Therefore, he was tasked with actively preparing for it. Subsequently, the regulations of the Bureau were promulgated, and considering that he had more than 30 years of experience in handling postal matters, and that he had gained much knowledge of savings and remittance matters through his overseas investigations, he was selected to concurrently serve as the Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, while the Vice Minister Wei Yifu temporarily served as the Director-General of the Postal Bureau. It was reported to the Executive Yuan for approval. Since the Bureau was established on March 15th of last year, it has only been a few months, but the results have been good. Judging from its development, it is not enough to have a dedicated person in charge to take on this important task. It is proposed to transfer him to serve exclusively as the Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, and to remove him from his original position as Director of the Postal Department and concurrently Director-General of the Postal Bureau, in order to focus his responsibilities. For the vacant position of Director of the Postal Department, there is Long Dafu, the current chief of the first section of the Postal Department, who is experienced and capable and has been handling postal affairs for many years, and his qualifications are very deep. It is proposed to appoint him as Director of the Postal Department. For the vacant position of Director-General of the Postal Bureau, there is Qian Chunqi, a technician with excellent talent and learning, who served as a counselor to Representative Liu at the Universal Postal Union Congress last year and has made many plans for postal reform since returning to China. It is proposed to transfer him to be Director-General of the Postal Bureau. We ask that the Executive Yuan review and implement the above reasons for the sake of public convenience."

### Anhui People Again Request the Abolition of Salt Surcharges 67

In order to raise funds for the provincial defense army, the Anhui Provincial Government collected a surcharge on salt tax in northern and southern Anhui of 2.4 yuan per stone. The people of Anhui, unable to bear the burden, publicly elected Peng Zhuoru, Yang Yaonan, and others as representatives from the mass organizations of 21 counties in northern Anhui to petition in Beijing. Although the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance repeatedly issued orders to abolish it, the Anhui Provincial Government did not comply. Recently, it has been vigorously enforced and forced to pay. The representatives, feeling the urgency, sent another telegram to the central government yesterday, appealing for a strict order to be issued to the Anhui Provincial Government to implement the abolition, and would not stop until the goal was achieved. The telegram is recorded below: "Chairman of the National Government and Premier of the Executive Yuan Jiang, Minister of Finance Song, for your consideration. We, the representatives, were publicly elected by the mass organizations of 21 counties in northern Anhui to petition in Beijing for the abolition of the salt surcharge in Anhui Province. We have repeatedly petitioned and have been repeatedly ordered by your esteemed Executive Yuan and Ministry to abolish it. All the people of Anhui are deeply grateful. We, the representatives, should have waited quietly for the resolution, how dare we bother you again? However, we have just received a letter from Wabao stating that the Bengbu Bureau has not complied with the order to abolish the salt surcharge and has reported it, and there are telegrams about sealing salt warehouses and arresting the ringleaders. Merchants and citizens are in a state of panic. Bengbu is located in the central hub of the southern section of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, and commerce is concentrated there. Salt and grain have always been fundamental. If salt and grain are suddenly heavily taxed, merchants will not dare to risk investing in transportation, and all industries will be shut down. The livelihood of tens of millions of laborers will be cut off. At a time when the communists are lurking, if an accident occurs, the impact on local security will be enormous. The central government rules the provinces, and the provinces rule the counties. This is the legal procedure. Now, the Anhui Provincial Government has arbitrarily added a salt surcharge, disrupting the salt administration, violating the law, and acting willfully, causing the central government's policy of abolishing likin to be unable to be implemented. Anhui Province is in a state of decline, and the people's livelihood has been suffering for a long time. How can the people recognize this illegal surcharge, which adds millions of burdens every year? We, the representatives, came to Beijing to petition, determined to sacrifice ourselves. Threats and inducements are of no concern to us. We know that this action will inevitably incur the resentment of the provincial government, and it will be easy to find fault in the future. However, we, the representatives, are pleading for the people, concerning the greatest suffering of the people in 21 counties. Even if we risk execution, we will not hesitate. Therefore, we are submitting this report again, hoping that the Chairman and your esteemed Ministry will quickly telegraph the Anhui Provincial Government, ordering them to abolish this salt surcharge immediately, in order to uphold the law and alleviate the people's hardship. We await your orders with utmost fear and trepidation. Peng Zhuoru, Yang Yaonan, and others, representatives of the petitioning group of the people of 21 counties in northern Anhui, together with Qiu Yuzhou and Xiang Yuncheng, and others of the Bengbu Chamber of Commerce, the Huai Salt Transport Merchants Association, and the Salt Industry Association, bow respectfully."

### Qingdao Consolidated Tax Bureau Prepares to Start Collecting Taxes 68

Implementation to Begin on February 1st

Registration of Existing Inventory and Payment of Supplementary Taxes

Qingdao Communication: Since its establishment, the Qingdao Luyu Consolidated Tax Bureau has continued to collect taxes on the original two items, cigarettes and wheat flour, and has not yet begun to collect taxes on the three newly added items, cotton yarn, cement, and matches. Now, the bureau has received a telegram order from the Ministry of Finance, approving the implementation of the collection of the consolidated tax on all three unhandled items starting on February 1st. After receiving the order, Director Pan Yaorong has ordered his subordinates to prepare accordingly and decided to start collecting taxes on February 1st. In addition to reporting the handling situation to the Ministry of Finance, he also notified the factories concerned to comply. All the resident factory staff have also been announced and assigned to the factories to take up their duties. The letter from the bureau to the Qingdao Chamber of Commerce and the supplementary tax measures are recorded below:

Letter to the Chamber of Commerce: This bureau previously received instructions from the Ministry of Finance to handle the consolidated tax on cotton yarn, matches, and cement in Shandong and Henan, and immediately prepared to proceed. Now, it has been completed and the collection will begin on February 1st of this year. However, it has been discovered that goods without tax bills or code symbols will be punished in accordance with the tax evasion regulations. If the supplementary tax measures are not notified in advance, merchants may suffer unexpected losses, which is not the intention of this bureau to care for the merchants. Therefore, four supplementary tax measures for cotton yarn, matches, and cement are formulated. In addition to public announcements and separate letters, the text of the measures is hereby sent to your association for your information. Please assist and notify merchants and others to comply.

Supplementary tax measures: (1) The inventory of cotton yarn, matches, and cement in various factories that has not been shipped out should be stopped from moving three days before the start of collection, and the resident factory staff should be allowed to check and register. When the goods are shipped out, the consolidated tax should be paid in accordance with the prescribed procedures. (2) The inventory in various customs warehouses should also be stopped from moving three days before the start of collection. The warehouse manager and the consigning merchants should report to the resident customs office and allow them to check and register. The consolidated tax should be paid up on the day of collection, and the tax bill should be issued after printing the inspection code and stamping the symbol, and then the goods can be picked up. (3) The stock of goods sold by merchants or wholesalers should also be stopped from moving three days before the start of collection, but each merchant is allowed to dismantle a certain amount of goods for retail, but must report the number of pieces in advance and pay the supplementary tax on the day of collection. (4) Goods stored in other warehouses (various banks or companies) by factories due to loans or other reasons should also be stopped from moving three days before the start of collection. The resident factory staff should check the number and pay the supplementary tax at the management office in charge on the day of collection, and then print the original factory inspection code and stamp the symbol. The tax bill may be issued as a general tax bill first, and then a separate transportation bill may be issued when sold in the future, or the factory may request to issue a zero-number tax bill at its discretion. (January 30th)

Changes in the Chinese Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway 69

Guo Chongxi Dismissed, Fan Qiguang Succeeds

Harbin Dispatch: Since the incident on the Chinese Eastern Railway in 1929, the positions and powers of key personnel on the railway, such as the Director and Department Heads, have been different from those of ordinary transportation agencies with only specialized skills. They must possess both transportation and diplomatic acumen to handle matters effectively. Without transportation knowledge, it is increasingly impossible to cope with the actions of the Russians in the vast Russian sphere of influence, and the Russian side will inevitably act unilaterally, disregarding the Chinese side. Without diplomatic experience, it is difficult to deal with the Russians' numerous cunning schemes when an incident occurs. This is especially necessary for the Director, because the Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau system is inherently abnormal. The Russian side has one Director and one Deputy Director, while the Chinese side has only one Deputy Director as assistant. Without a capable person, there is no opportunity to speak or ask questions. After the 1929 incident, former Director Lü Ronghuan issued a statement blaming Chinese Deputy Director Guo Chongxi, saying that he was weak and incompetent. Although not entirely true, Guo's timidity caused problems not infrequently. After the signing of the Khabarovsk Protocol and the restoration of the Chinese Eastern Railway to its original state, Guo, the Director who was dismissed by Lü Ronghuan, also benefited from Russian influence and was restored to his original position. Last spring, when Mo Dehui came to take office as Supervisor, he planned to remove Guo for his poor performance. Later, he went to Russia and had no time for this. When Mo returned to China before the New Year, Guo, knowing that he was inevitable, submitted his resignation in advance. Mo then forwarded it to the Ministry of Railways and the Northeast Transportation Committee for approval. On the 18th of this month, Mo went from Harbin to Liaoning to personally report to Zhang Xueliang. Zhang also considered the powers and status of the Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway to be important and instructed to select diplomatic talent for the position. There was discussion about transferring the current Acting Chairman of the Chinese Eastern Railway, Li Shaogeng, but since Mo was still going to Russia for meetings and the Acting Chairman was also important, they discussed the next best option. It was decided to transfer Fan Qiguang, a Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway, to fill the position. Fan had served as Consul in Boli (Khabarovsk) and Heihe, Russia, and as a Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway for many years. Choosing the right person for the job, it was deemed appropriate. Therefore, on the 20th of this month, Mo summoned Li and Fan to meet Zhang Xueliang and immediately telegraphed the Ministry of Railways to issue an official announcement. As for Fan's vacant Director position, it will be filled by Zhang Shou Zeng, the current Director of the Heihe Municipal Preparatory Office. This must also be officially announced by the Ministry of Railways. Although Guo Chongxi has not yet handed over his duties, he is no longer handling affairs. Several Department Heads related to Guo are also rushing to hand over their duties. In less than ten days, the situation on the Chinese Eastern Railway will have a new look. (January 29th)

Establishment of Weather Stations in Jiangsu Province 70

Branch Stations Established in Various Counties, Water Gauges Installed in Counties Near Water

Predicting Weather Changes for the Next 24 Hours

The Jiangsu Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau, recognizing that weather changes are closely related to water conservancy, agriculture, transportation, and other aspects, has established a weather station within the bureau. Branch weather stations will be established in the construction bureaus of various counties, and water gauges will be set up along the Yangtze River and the Grand Canal to observe water levels. It is reported that the weather instruments for the main and branch stations were ordered from famous manufacturers in England and Germany and have been arriving continuously. Once they are fully installed, observations will begin. The results will be reported twice daily, in the morning and afternoon, by the provincial radio station to the Nanjing Central Station, the Xujiahui Station in Shanghai, the Qingdao Special Municipality, the Shandong Construction Department, and other weather stations in the country for reference. The daily weather forecast for the next 24 hours in Zhenjiang will be published in newspapers after several days of testing.

Also, the clocks in the provincial capital are inconsistent and lack standardization, causing inconvenience to all sectors. It is reported that the station is studying the use of noon cannons or other methods to provide a standard for timekeeping for all sectors.

Mo Dehui Travels South from Shenyang 71

Shenyang Dispatch: Mo Dehui, the plenipotentiary representative for the Sino-Soviet Conference, arrived in Shenyang a few days ago to pay respects to Deputy Commander Zhang. He then went to Tanggangzi with his secretary for rest. He telegraphed Foreign Minister Wang, saying, "Minister Wang Rutang, my dear brother, I hope this reaches you well. I am still suffering from skin disease and insomnia, and plan to go to the hot springs for a few days to recuperate, and will come south immediately. I expect to arrive in Beijing around the end of the month. I am sending this telegram in advance." Now, because Mo is eager to go south, he returned to Shenyang on the 24th. He has been in consultation with Deputy Commander Zhang and various administrative committee members for several days. By the 27th, the opinions of the leaders had converged, and Mo's mission in Shenyang was completed. He left Shenyang south today (30th) at 7:00 PM with Deputy Foreign Minister Wang Jiazhen, Special Commissioner Li Chen, Secretary Wu Zesheng, and others. Many important figures in the political world went to the station to see him off. It is reported that Mo will not delay in Tianjin and will immediately enter Beijing. (30th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 72

A Fifteen-Year-Old Girl Seduced and Detained: Bian Qiaolin, a girl from Wuxi residing in Sijing Town, is only fifteen years old and has some beauty. She was seduced by Zhang Shuming of the Sijing Rope Shop a few days ago, causing inflammation of her lower body. Her family discovered this and reported it to the local branch station, requesting an investigation. Officer Zhang ordered the police to arrest Zhang. Because the case involved allegations of rape and was a criminal matter, it was prepared and sent to Songjiang and then to the Prosecutor's Office for investigation. The girl, Bian Qiaolin, was transferred to Songjiang Hospital for examination to determine if she was a virgin. It is reported that the hospital has confirmed and submitted its findings for review.

A Glimpse of Banditry in Punan: Bandits are rampant in various towns in Punan, and the people are living in misery. Robberies and kidnappings are heard of almost daily. The night before last (1st), more than ten bandits suddenly came to the home of Zhang Xiangyu in Xiaheng Southwest of Tinglin, each carrying sharp knives and axes, and entered to commit robbery. During the commotion, Xie Zikun, a neighbor, heard the noise and went out to investigate, but was slashed by a bandit guarding the area, causing serious injuries. However, the losses were not too great because the bandits, seeing that they had caused trouble, hastily fled. It is also reported that a few days ago, dozens of bandits wearing copper basin hats and white edges suddenly came to the Qianxiang area, divided into the Public Security Bureau and the District Office, intending to coerce the leaders. However, the town merchants, seeing the situation, were alarmed and wanted to go to the door, but were stopped by the bandits, who claimed, "We are not local bandits, nor are we kidnappers. We are here to raise funds." They ordered the pointing out of more than thirty wealthy households in the town, wanting to raise 12,000 yuan. As a result, in addition to looting police weapons, they also took away a list of wealthy households.

Fengxian 73

The Leader of a Kidnapping Gang Arrested in Shanghai: Chen Jinfang, the Chief Inspector of the County Public Security Bureau, learned that the leader of the kidnapping gang that occurred at Pan Bosong's home in Huaantou, Xiaotang, was hiding in the Shanghai Concession. Yesterday (1st), he took police officers to Shanghai and reported to the local police station. Two men from Jiangbei, Jiang Huanzhang and Chen Sishan (nicknamed "Big Head"), were arrested in houses at 602 Xiaoshadu Road in the Public Concession and in Yichang Lane. However, because they did not bring official documents in haste, they will go to transfer them tomorrow. The five previously arrested kidnappers, Hu Dengkui, Jiang Dahua, and the kidnap victim Wang Qisong, were sent to Kunshan County, where the crime occurred, yesterday (2nd) by the county police to be interrogated together.

Jinshan 74

Continued Report on the Rampant Bandits in Southern Jinshan: The rampant bandits in the Shantang area of southern Jinshan have been reported in this newspaper many times. In the last four days, six more cases have occurred: (1) The homes of Wang Peihe, Li Axiao, and Qi in Sanbang, south of Ganxiang, were all intimidated by Xu Buming (also known as Tailor Ajin) and Monk Luo, subordinates of Taibao Ashu, on the 29th of last month, and each was defrauded of 300-400 yuan. (2) The home of Lu Xinqing, a farmer in Beimo Ku, was suddenly invaded by more than twenty bandits on the night of the 30th. They openly held weapons, broke down the door, wantonly searched, and severely beat Xinqing, forcing him to reveal where he hid his silver, causing Xinqing to be injured all over his body. After three days, he eventually died from his injuries. (3) The homes of the fifth and second brothers of Zhu Yunsheng in Daochangjing were also forced to borrow more than 200 yuan each by the bandits Monk Luo and others on the 31st. (4) The home of Huang Sanquan in front of Nanmo Ku, who was forced to borrow a large sum by Taibao Ashu last summer, was visited again by two bandits sent by Tailor Ajin on the 1st. They carried a boxed cannon and a threatening letter, forcing him to borrow 800 yuan and setting a deadline of 2:00 PM the next day to meet at Huangtan Bridge. (5) The home of Chen Atu, a farmer west of Yaojiakan, was also forced to borrow 200 yuan by the bandits Monk Luo and others on the same day. (6) Shanzhuan, half a li west of Kongjiaque, has always been a frequent haunt of bandits. The local village head, Zhu Yizhai, has considerable wealth, making him a target for bandits. On the evening of January 5th, the bandits Monk Luo and others robbed him severely and killed his elderly wife, who was in her seventies. Unexpectedly, the bandits were not satisfied and, yesterday evening (1st) at dusk, Monk Luo led more than twenty bandits, each carrying pistols, boxed cannons, and other weapons, and rushed in. Seeing that there were no more valuables to loot, they kidnapped his son, Da Jie, and headed northwest.

Suzhou 75

Former Magistrate of Ganyu County Petitions for Return of Property: Wang Zuoliang, the former Magistrate of Ganyu County, was detained and sent to the High Court for trial on charges of counter-revolution. His property was sealed. Later, the High Court ruled him not guilty, but the prosecutor appealed to the Supreme Court. In October of last year, the case was sent back to the High Court for retrial. After the trial, he was again found not guilty. The appeal period of more than three months has passed. Wang Zuoliang submitted a petition to the High Court on the 2nd, requesting the return of his sealed property to maintain his livelihood.

Verdict in Seduction of a Young Girl Case: Lan Xufang, the 20-year-old daughter of Lan Lianchen of No. 1 Huajin Lane in Shanghai, fell in love with Chen Mingqi against her parents' wishes. They married on October 9, 1930, at the Cadet Hotel on Cadet Road. Lan Lianchen discovered this and brought Chen Mingqi to the Shanghai District Court, accusing him of seducing a young girl. The Shanghai District Court sentenced Chen to six months in prison. Chen appealed to the High Court. Yesterday afternoon (3rd), the Second Criminal Court pronounced its verdict, rejecting the appeal.

Wuxi 76

Communist from Jiangyin Arrested in Wuxi: Lu Zibao, a famous communist leader from Jiangyin, was arrested and executed in that county. His followers, Wang Fuquan and others, continued to commit murder and arson in the county. Qian Tianxiong, the captain of the water patrol team of the local county police brigade, received a report from an informant stating that Wang Fuquan, a communist from Jiangyin, had fled to Suzhou last month, robbed a family named Mao in Huqiu, and had now come to Wuxi, hiding in a certain place in the South Gate of the county. He requested that a team be dispatched to arrest him. After receiving the report, Captain Qian, together with Liao Dajin, the leader of the detective team, led detectives to search for him but did not find him. They then went to patrol the area around the road and arrested the bandit Wang Fuquan near the Xiangzhong Hotel. During interrogation, Wang confessed that he was from Jiangyin, 38 years old, and admitted to robbing the Mao family in Huqiu, Suzhou, with six accomplices, dividing the spoils and using them. He also confessed that after the execution of the bandit leader Lu Zibao, he and his accomplices joined a certain leader of the Red Army in Jiangyin and possessed four boxed pistols. After receiving the confession, Captain Qian prepared a document yesterday (3rd) and submitted it to the Brigade Headquarters, which forwarded it to the County Court for trial.

The County Court Officially Opens for Business: The County Court of Wuxi has been established since the 24th of last month. In addition to the Prosecutor's Office, which had already opened, the court section officially began operations yesterday, accepting civil and criminal lawsuits.

Another Thief Alarm in Kaihua Township: Several robberies have occurred in Kaihua Township of Wuxi County in recent days, and none have been solved. Unexpectedly, four or five bandits came to the home of Tao Xiqing, a villager in Tashi, and used a ladder to climb onto the roof, intending to enter and commit robbery. Tao Xiqing heard the sound of tiles and knew that thieves were coming. He loudly banged on a tin box. Neighbors heard the sound and gathered to catch the thieves. The thieves were extremely panicked and fled. Afterwards, two straw hats left behind by the thieves were found.

Collection of Storefront Rent Donation in the Urban Area: The County Government previously received an order from the Department of Civil Affairs instructing it to investigate and report when the storefront rent donation in the urban area was approved for collection, how it has been collected in the past, how much is collected annually, and what it is used for. The County Government immediately sent a letter to the City Property Management Committee for investigation and reporting. The City Property Management Committee replied that the storefront rent donation in the urban area has been collected by local self-government organizations since the late Qing Dynasty during the preparation for self-government, and is specifically used for police expenses. In September of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), the former Municipal Preparatory Office revised the regulations for collecting storefront rent donations, which were approved by the Department of Civil Affairs under Order No. 22325. Calculated at 10% of the actual rent, the monthly amount to be collected in the urban area is 5,390.274 yuan, but the average actual monthly collection is only more than 5,000 yuan, which is not enough to cover the 5,500 yuan allocated monthly for urban public security expenses. Yesterday, the situation was reported to the County Government, along with the regulations for collecting storefront rent donations, for forwarding to the Department of Civil Affairs for record.

Wujiang 77

Water Patrol Team Rescues Kidnap Victim: The County Water Patrol Team exchanged fire with bandits in Taikang New Harbor at 12:00 AM last night, captured one bandit boat, two rifles, and one Wang Shoushan, who was watching the boat. They also rescued Xu Wenlong, a kidnap victim from Hengdu District of the county. All were sent to the county for interrogation today.

Meeting of the Security Committee: Yesterday, the County Government of Wujiang convened a meeting of the County Security Committee to discuss the following proposals: (1) Regarding the Department's order to formally organize the security corps as a key matter, it was decided to complete the organization and report it by the end of February of this year. (2) Regarding when to organize and establish the General Headquarters because the funds have not been allocated and the Chief Training Officer has not been appointed, it was decided to organize and establish the General Headquarters immediately. The County Magistrate will urge the Property Management Office to advance the funds and select suitable talent to serve as Training Officers.

Changzhou 78

Chamber of Commerce Cables Request to Revise Business Tax Rate: The Wuyi County Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Executive Yuan of the Nanjing National Government and the Ministry of Finance yesterday (2nd), stating that according to Article 4 of the Outline for the Collection of Business Tax in Various Provinces promulgated by the Executive Yuan, the business tax rate should be calculated and collected at a rate of per mille based on the taxable standard and should not exceed 2 per mille. Recently, it was read in the newspaper that the tax rates stipulated in the Jiangsu Province Business Tax Regulations were more than ten times higher than the outline, which was clearly inconsistent with the central government's orders. All businesses were alarmed and appealed, requesting a reduction or exemption to alleviate business difficulties. In recent years, business conditions have been depressed, and all industries have been struggling. Bankruptcies and closures have been frequently heard of. Even if the government does not provide relief, it should show sympathy and reduce taxes to allow for recovery. Now, it is still violating the principles of the outline promulgated by the Executive Yuan and increasing the burden on businesses and the people, which is not a way to save the people and support businesses. Therefore, we specially telegraph the Executive Yuan and the Ministry, humbly asking you to consider the difficulties of businesses and quickly order the Jiangsu Provincial Government to revise the tax rate according to the outline, so that the businesses and the people who are on the verge of collapse can catch their breath.

Detective Team Returned to the Command of the County Government: The Wuyi Public Security Bureau's Detective Team was previously decided by the local conference to be transferred to the County Government for management. County Magistrate Zhang, based on the proposal, ordered the Public Security Bureau Director to transfer the team to the County Government for close command starting from February 1st. The Public Security Bureau, upon receiving the order, is preparing for the transfer. Xu Zusheng Accused of Misappropriating Construction Funds: The Jiangsu Construction Department recently received a report from Zhang Hongjun, the concurrent Director of the Zhenjiang County and Yangzhong Construction Bureau, forwarding a report from Cui Hualiang, a technician from Yangzhong County, accusing Xu Zusheng, the former Magistrate of Yangzhong County, of misappropriating more than 4,000 yuan in construction funds. After receiving the report, the Construction Department has reportedly forwarded it to the Department of Civil Affairs for investigation.

All five thatched houses were destroyed without a trace, and all the goods in the houses were burned. Two yellow oxen used for stomping paper also suffered from the fire. One died on the spot, and the other only had a breath left. By the time the fire engines from various districts arrived, the fire had been extinguished.

Road Workers Forcibly Seize Smuggled Salt: Two anti-smuggling police officers from the Pinghu Chamber of Commerce seized a load of smuggled salt outside the North River Tower of the South Gate on the 1st and were preparing to hand it over to the authorities. Hangzhou Tap Water Implemented Trial Water: The Hangzhou Tap Water Preparatory Committee has recently buried a section of water pipes from outside Gulou to Yan Gong Lane, which has been completed. Therefore, it is proposed to ask the Municipal Government to straighten Yan Guan Lane to facilitate progress. Construction can begin in a few days.

Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom Frost Red 85

▲Money that can be accumulated but not spent inevitably turns one into a miser. Money that can be spent but not accumulated inevitably turns one into a spendthrift.

▲By not setting foot in places of pleasure, gambling, etc., one not only cherishes wealth but also cherishes one's body. By paying attention to useful books, whether Chinese or Western, one not only increases wisdom but also increases virtue.

▲Knowing the bitterness of asking for help from others, one should be even more frugal when one has extra money. Knowing the difficulty of entrusting others to handle matters, those who are in position should not be greedy for more.

▲Miserly families often produce prodigal sons. Acrimonious children are sure to be failures.

▲When one is in the world, one must have pride, but not arrogance. When parents love their children, they do not need to leave them property, but they must give them skills.

▲Instead of haggling over every penny in the vegetable market, why not eat one less bite yourself? Instead of arguing red-faced with a rickshaw puller over the fare, why not walk a few more steps yourself?

▲Heaven and earth are the lodging places of all things, so great wealth and honor are just empty dreams. Why take them too seriously? Time is a passerby for a hundred generations, so whether one is a saint or a madman, one should seize every moment. How can one not cherish it?

▲A single word of greed can lead to the bankruptcy and ruin of the rich. A single word of diligence can enable the poor to start a business and prosper.

▲Not reading dead books is true learning. Being able to recognize small resentments is called a great hero.

▲Those who are content always have more joy. Those who are never content have little happiness throughout the year.

▲Those who like to talk about the shortcomings of others behind their backs are certainly not upright people. I should be careful in dealing with them. Those who can point out my faults to my face are certainly warm-hearted people. I should befriend them well.

▲Entering a good family is like sitting in the spring breeze, making one feel refreshed. Reading bad novels is like falling into a demon's lair, making one's mind confused.

▲Flowers are best when half-open. One should leave some room when drinking alcohol.

Strange Customs of Mongolia Zhao Lanhuan 86

Yesterday, I attended a friend's banquet and met an old man in his sixties. He claimed to have just returned from the northern border. During the banquet, he spoke at length about the customs of Inner Mongolia, as if they were his own family treasures. I will record its strange points to share with readers.

▲Difficulty in Asking for Directions: The most inconvenient thing for travelers entering Mongolia for the first time is the difficulty in asking for directions. Mongolians consider it shameful to speak Chinese and delightful for Chinese to speak Mongolian well. Chinese who speak Mongolian well will certainly receive enthusiastic hospitality wherever they go. If one speaks Chinese to ask for directions, Mongolians will certainly ignore them, even if one begs on one's knees.

▲Lamas in Power: The administrative power of all Mongolian tribes is controlled by lamas. Once orders are issued, the people must obey. Moreover, Mongolians worship lamas, so if there are two sons, one must be chosen to become a lama. Although restricted by religious rules and not allowed to marry, the material benefits are very generous, and there is hope of holding great power in the future. Therefore, Mongolians see becoming a lama as a shortcut to promotion and wealth. There are no doctors in Mongolia. When someone is sick, the lama will diagnose them, often using tree bark and animal bones as medicine, and many recover safely.

▲The Custom of Polygamy: Mongolia is a vast desert, but the water and grass are lush, making it easy for nomads to live. Most of the people make a living from this, and there are very few idlers. Women work especially hard. Men only engage in outdoor herding, while women, in addition to managing household affairs, also milk livestock in the morning and evening. The wealthy often marry multiple wives and concubines to share the work, and there is no distinction between wives and concubines.

▲Trade by Barter: Any Chinese who are familiar with Mongolian customs will profit when they go to do business. Trade is conducted by barter, and very little is done with cash. The method is to first distribute goods to Mongolians at the beginning of the year, and in the winter, take livestock, bones, leather, fur, and other items of equivalent value. Mongolians

Food Named After Spring: Yang Yi Xiao 87

Spring Everlasting (Chun Bu Lao): Mustard greens are pickled and stored for over a month, removing the pungent taste. They are eaten as an appetizer,

remarkably delicious.

Spring Bamboo Shoots: The shells of spring bamboo shoots are peeled off, and the tips are picked. They are stir-fried with shrimp roe, soy sauce, and a little lard, then removed after two or three stirs. They are extraordinarily tender.

Spring Rolls: Fillings of leek sprouts and shredded pork are wrapped in wrappers to form rolls. They are placed in a lard wok and fried until golden brown on both sides. They are crispy and delicious.

▲ Spring Pancakes: Finely shred radish and mix with flour and salt. Fry in an oil wok until cooked and eat immediately, known as "biting the spring."

Honest and reliable, with very little dispute, it is said.

▲ An Unconventional Funeral: Mongolian funerals are particularly strange. When someone dies, regardless of age, they are not placed in a coffin. Instead, the body is moved to a wilderness area frequented by wolves, tigers, and leopards to satisfy their hunger. After a few days, if the body has been eaten by wild animals, it is said that the person has ascended to heaven. Otherwise, it is said that the person was extremely sinful, and the whole family considers it unlucky, it is said.

Thirty-Year-Old Blind Man Regains His Sight in Autumn 88

In Poet's Valley, America, there is a blind merchant named Fish. J.F. Fish lost his sight due to eye disease thirty years ago. On the evening of a certain day in early July of last year, he suddenly felt something in front of him, gradually becoming clear. Both eyes actually regained their sight. Because of the interesting nature of this event, he wrote it down.

▲ Wedding Bliss Turns to Calamity: Thirty-one years ago today (i.e., 1899), Fish had just graduated from university and married his beloved in Poet's Valley. They went to Wahawa for their honeymoon. One day, while walking in the countryside with his wife, they rested under a large tree. Suddenly, a branch broke off and fell to the ground, hitting the groom's eye and injuring it. The bride accompanied him home and sought medical treatment, but it was ineffective, and he became blind. Over the years, he had spent over 50,000 gold coins on medical expenses to treat his eyes, but to no avail. Now, when all hope was lost, he suddenly regained his sight, which is quite remarkable.

▲ Interesting Dark Life: Fish, a promising young man, suddenly suffered the pain of blindness. His life was dark, and he had no joy in living. One can imagine. However, he was quite content in his thirty years of darkness. He had profound knowledge to interact with society. He had no worries about the family being well-fed and clothed. He also had a virtuous wife who served him every day. He had no internal worries and enjoyed family happiness. Although his eyes were blind, his heart was happy. One evening, while sitting on the side of the courtyard, his wife was reciting a novel for him. Fish suddenly felt a slight light shining in front of him. The light gradually increased. Suddenly, he saw a chair in the darkness. After a long time, he saw a picture. After a long time, he saw his wife sitting beside him. Fish was extremely shocked and stood up, saying, "The world has turned upside down! Where shall I place myself? Wife, I see you!" Then they hugged and kissed, and cried, "Thirty years of separation, I can see you again. God is so merciful." The next day, he told his relatives and friends. His relatives and friends were also overjoyed and threw a party to celebrate. At the banquet, Fish said to the crowd, "After twenty years of separation, your faces are no longer the same as before. The social situation has also been completely renewed, very different from before. Recalling the situation thirty years ago is like another lifetime. My heart is extremely happy. Please offer sincere thanks to God for me."

Viewing a Honeybee Painting Exhibition and Listening to Ice Being Born 89

Parisian Tales (22) Liu Ceng Ji in Paris 90

Thirteen, The Botanical Garden

Almost every city in France with a university has a very complete botanical garden (jardindesplantes), the scale of which is naturally larger and more complete than those in the provinces.

Coming out of the University of Paris, walk along Rue Saint-Jacques to the bank of the Seine. Turn and walk east along the riverbank. In a dozen minutes, you will reach the west gate of the Botanical Garden. A leisurely stroll along the riverbank is already very refreshing. But after you enter the Botanical Garden, your mind will be even lighter. In the fifth arrondissement, where most students live, the Botanical Garden can be considered the second most suitable place for students to rest, after the Luxembourg Gardens that I mentioned earlier.

The Botanical Garden is not as large as the Luxembourg Gardens in area, and the scenery is far less beautiful than the Luxembourg Gardens. But this place has a benefit that ordinary parks do not have. You can gain a lot of knowledge by walking around here. There are more than 11,000 kinds of plants in this garden, all categorized scientifically. In front of each plant is a sign indicating its scientific name, common name, and origin, etc. Almost all kinds of different plants from all over the world have one or two specimens. Walking around here is like surveying the plants of the world.

The garden also has a zoo attached, but you have to buy a separate ticket to enter. There are also several kinds of animals inside that Chinese people rarely see. But this zoo is ultimately an ancillary nature and not very large. There is another complete large zoo outside the city of Paris. I will introduce it in a separate article later.

Bees are certainly good at making honey. A painting society adopts the name "Bee," and its diligence in production can be imagined. The gentlemen of the Bee Society, at the end of the Gengwu year, when the wind and snow were fierce, to pass the cold, opened the New World Hotel and gathered in a room. They sat around the stove, brewed wine, and mixed powder to prepare pigments. The elegance of the art world was exhausted. After a dozen days, they examined their paintings and obtained 200 pieces of fine art, which were publicly exhibited. I, Yu Dao, passed by Xizang Road and took the opportunity to admire them. I exclaimed in admiration. Zhang Shanzi's painting of tigers had the menacing power to pounce on people. Combined with Ma Qizhou's embellishment of trees and rocks, the craftsmanship was equally matched. Ye Weishen's painting of white doves was complemented by Wang Shizi's roses, with elegant colors and exquisite charm. Shang Shengbo's painting "Wine and Meat Friends" showed a piece of fatty meat and a mound of yellow soil, with a unique flavor. Sun Xueni's "Firewood and Rice Couple" showed a rice basket and a bundle of firewood, also quite wonderful. Xi Yanzi titled a poem, saying, "I heard that it is not easy to live in Chang'an, firewood is like jade cinnamon, and rice is like pearls. I laugh at the poor couple who guard their old house in the wind and snow." Yanzi has been wandering in recent years, and his poems are full of complaints. The old dream of black clothes makes him unconsciously sigh deeply. Others, such as Xiong Songquan's painting of lions, Ma Mengrong's red carp, and Shen Jianzhi and He Tianjian's landscapes, competed for beauty, which is worth mentioning. As for the "Three Friends of Winter," Zheng Wuchang painted pines, Qian Shoutie painted plums, with misty smoke and delicate elegance, and Sun Xueni's double-hooked new bamboo, with lush green depths and dense thickets, creating the sound of wind through the pines. It is truly rare. I especially admire Ye Weishen's large horizontal landscape painting, with its lofty spirit and splashed ink. Du Fu's poem "The walls are covered with scenes of Xiao and Xiang" seems to be written for this painting. In terms of its charm, it is between Xiangyang and bitter gourd, but it is not limited to one style. It is transformed with brushstrokes, so in the midst of the ancient and vigorous, it also obtains a clear, exquisite, and charming style. Xie Yucen, Wang Geshan, and Zheng Wuchang each wrote a poem to praise it. The diligent bees, whose carving is as refined as described above, I hope that the literary and artistic world of our East will also rely on the support of these gentlemen.

▲ Plum News: In the past, Fan Chengda wrote a preface to the Plum Manual, calling plums the most precious thing in the world. He also said that plums are superior in charm and high in character. Therefore, the most prized plums are those with a horizontal, oblique, sparse, and elegant shape, with old trunks and forked branches. Famous sages such as Song Guangping, Du Shaoling, and Lin Hejing all had diplomatic relations with plums, which is reasonable. Now there are plums produced by Xiaoguanyuan, such as Shunfeng plums, Jianjin plums, Gubengpi plums, Hejing pine bamboo plum, peony camellia plum, and other bonsai, each with its own posture. Since they were put on the market, buyers have flocked to them. The retail departments at the west entrance of the Great World on Avenue Edward VII and the distribution point next to the Shishi Xinbao on Wangping Street are all overwhelmed, it is said. (Liu Gong)

Warmth in the Heart (363) Bao Tianxiao 91

Chapter 17: The Art of Preserving Youthful Looks with Emerald Black Eyebrows, Continuing Life is Impossible with a Golden Market of Fine Horses

Ason’s several Hansom cabs were all spruced up exceptionally well. The body of the carriage was lacquered to be immaculate, so shiny it could be used as a mirror. The cushions were all made of royal blue satin and daffodil-yellow satin, embroidered with many colorful flowers. The reins were made of green silk ribbon. The carriage was equipped with a soft rattan whip that was over ten feet long, tied with alternating blue and white silk, section by section, also decorated with red, purple, yellow, and green tassels, fluttering in the wind, looking even more beautiful in the shadow of the setting sun. The carriage was not only lightweight, but also harnessed to a black-cloud piebald horse, whose four hooves kicked up the wind, galloping as fast as a cloud dragon. The horse was as nimble and energetic as its driver. During the third month's excursions to Longhua to see the peach blossoms, and the New Year's five-day head start on the circular route, to show off, and the spring and autumn racing seasons, these fashionable gentlemen from the "Tangzi" establishments would all vie to ride Ason’s carriage. On those days, Ason's limelight was even stronger. The Hansom cab was light and small, unable to seat many people, at most accommodating three. It was best to sit shoulder to shoulder with the coachman, letting the coachman hold the reins. Otherwise, if two female companions were seated in the front, the coachman could still have a seat from behind and pull the reins through the gaps between the shoulders of the two women in the front. Hua Yuanchun was someone who enjoyed showing off and had a competitive nature. She often learned to hold the reins herself, personally instructed by Ason, and gradually became close. Therefore, what others could not snatch, she had already snatched first. Hua Yuanchun got two people she liked. However, these two people could not meet. But she was unwilling to offend either of them or abandon either of them. It was like what Mencius said, "Fish, I desire; bear's paw, I also desire." This relied on the means of the "Tangzi" establishment. A single girl serves two clients. If she did not have the means, things could go wrong, leading to jealousy and disputes. The furnishings in the room would be smashed, and cups and dishes would fly everywhere, making it difficult to please both sides, forcing her into a corner with no way out, even to the point of swallowing raw opium to commit suicide. Girls with means could pour sweet talk on both sides. To Client A, she would make mountain oaths and sea alliances, claiming that he was the only one she loved most. To Client B, she would also point to the heavens and swear by the sun, saying that there was no one else but him. "Having seen the great sea, water is difficult to be anything else; except for Mount Wu, clouds are not clouds," was also one of their secrets. The first step was to make Client A unaware of Client B, and Client B unaware of Client A, creating an impression of separation. Even if the truth leaked out, she could still patch things up. To Client A, she would say that she was completely devoted to him. To Client B, she was merely being perfunctory. On the other hand, she would say the same to Client B. When they were bewitched by her, both Client A and Client B would believe her words. All the skilled people in the brothel could do this. Hua Yuanchun was naturally a famous courtesan in Shanghai at the time. Therefore, she could still drive side by side, even though her two beloved enemies were traveling on separate paths.

Wheat Market Softens 104

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning, prices continued to be lively due to continued absorption by inland buyers. However, traders and factories, having made a deal for 14,000 tons of Australian wheat at only 4.01 taels the day before yesterday, successively shorted large quantities, so prices gradually softened again for various months. By the afternoon opening, short sellers continued to release their stocks, and factories continued to make deals for foreign wheat, so selling was even more prevalent, and prices for all months softened further. According to this situation, once domestic prices improve, foreign wheat will come to be peddled. It is feared that if a surge of supply is encountered in the future, it will be difficult to avoid falling again. As a result, this month's contracts fell by 0.06 yuan compared to the previous day, March and April contracts fell by 0.04 yuan, May contracts fell by 0.02 yuan, June contracts fell by 0.03 yuan, and July contracts improved by 0.01 yuan.
