Business Tax Rates in Various Provinces 110

If They Exceed Regulations

They Should Be Revised Separately

Ministry of Finance Replies to Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Telegram

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously telegraphed the Ministry of Finance on the 29th of last month, stating that the business tax rates set by various provinces mostly exceeded the limitations of the guidelines issued by the Ministry, and specially requested that the Ministry of Finance strictly revise them during the review. It is now reported that the Chamber received a reply telegram from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, saying: "To the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, your telegram of the 29th is noted. Regarding the implementation of business taxes in various provinces and cities, if the proposed tax rates and collection methods for business classifications exceed the regulations of the outline and supplementary measures set by the Ministry, the Ministry will review and revise them separately when the province submits them for record, in order to comply with the original plan. As for business circles in various provinces, if they wish to participate with their opinions in advance, they can directly submit them to the competent authorities for approval. This is a special reply. Ministry of Finance."

Research Committee on Tax Regulations for Various Industries Writes Important Documents on Business Tax 111

▲Submitting Statements

The Research Committee on Tax Regulations for Various Industries of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a letter to Minister Song on the issue of business tax, and also sent letters to accountants Pan Xulun and Xu Yongzuo, submitting statements. The original letter is as follows:

▲Letter to Minister Song: "To Minister, the Committee previously determined that the business tax rates stipulated by Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces were too high, and the business community found it difficult to bear the burden, with Shanghai being the most affected. Representatives were dispatched to submit petitions, but as you were unwell, we were unable to meet you. We left the petition for your review, hoping you will examine it. The Likin system is harmful to merchants and detrimental to the country. You, with the greatest determination, demolished and cleared it. The people are benefiting, and it is the glory of the Party and the country. However, after abolishing Likin, it is necessary to find compensatory measures. The way to compensate is to increase taxes, so abolishing Likin and increasing taxes has become a consistent and related term for decades. This year, Likin was abolished and tariffs were increased simultaneously. Short-term gains were used to compensate for losses, and with the revenue from consolidated taxes, there is no need to worry about shortages. The so-called business tax is only used to compensate for the additional tax losses of various provinces after the abolition of Likin, and it must not be assumed that the entire Likin revenue of various provinces should be compensated by the business tax. This is evidenced by the speech of legislator Ma Yinchu at the Shanghai Party Headquarters, stating that Zhejiang province lost 1.4 million yuan after abolishing Likin, and is further evidenced by your approval to subsidize the administrative expenses of Hunan, Hubei, Henan, and Jiangxi provinces with monthly payments ranging from 300,000 to 100,000 yuan. However, the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have not paid attention to this point, and they have misunderstood the object. Therefore, the provincial financial authorities feel the hardship of having no rice to cook, and the tax rates are feared to be too low, while the merchants in the two provinces are panicked and running around, as stated in the joint telegram of the sixty chambers of commerce in Jiangsu and Zhejiang: 'We have just celebrated the abolition of Likin, and we are now subjected to harsh taxes.' The melons of the Yellow Terrace, how can they be picked again? Going further, the financial authorities of the two provinces, coming from the people, also know the hardships of the merchants, but they have to do so because the province must have administration, and administration requires expenses. What they silently understand in their hearts, but cannot express in words, is that the central government is being generous at the expense of the provinces, completely removing the financial resources of the local areas, and greatly increasing the revenue of the central government. Furthermore, some even informally tell the merchants this, so the merchants shift their blame from the inappropriateness of the tax rates stipulated by the two provinces to resentment towards the central government. In fact, the central government is determined to abolish Likin, and its grace is deeply rooted in the people. The promulgation of the business tax guidelines and supplementary measures is also well-defined and comprehensive. The only misunderstanding is that there is no clear regulation on the Likin losses that various provinces should compensate with the business tax. The Committee intends to request you to quickly order the relevant departments to clearly announce the amount of additional tax lost by each province and city due to the abolition of Likin, and to simultaneously notify each province and city to still base their drafting of business tax rates on the guidelines issued by the Yuan and the supplementary measures restrictions, to compensate for the inadequacy of the additional tax. Furthermore, please ask the central government to allocate funds to subsidize the provinces. As for the Likin regular tax, it will be compensated by the increased tariffs and the consolidated and special taxes. The provincial and municipal financial authorities need not worry too much about it. If this decree is issued this morning, we will see cheers thunderous, and the virtue of the Party-State and you will be forever engraved in our hearts. In addition, on the 3rd of this month, the newspaper reported your remarks, saying that the business tax rates of 2/1000 and 20/1000 are all extremely low tax rates. Considering your original intention, it is assumed that you consider extremely low tax rates to be compared to those in Europe and America. However, in terms of production, China is an extremely low-production country. In terms of people's lives, 99% of the Chinese people cannot even achieve an extremely low standard of living. It is obvious that extremely low tax rates must be levied on a country with extremely low production and a population with extremely low living standards. However, Article 4 of the Executive Yuan's Guidelines for the Collection of Business Tax in Various Provinces states that the tax rate for those levied on business turnover shall not exceed 2/1000. Article 8 of the Supplementary Measures states that the tax rate for those levied on capital shall not exceed 20/1000. What you call an extremely low tax rate is a comparison between China and other countries. The guidelines and supplementary measures, the so-called 'shall not exceed' and 'shall not exceed' are to limit the highest burden standard for the population with extremely low standards of living in an extremely low production country. Currently, the number of industries collecting business tax in Zhejiang province is eleven, and the number of industries collecting business tax in Jiangsu province is sixteen. Among the eleven and sixteen industries, only food, firewood, coal, and salt in the sales industry are taxed at 1/1000, while the rest are all above 2/1000. It is almost as if they recognize the highest limit previously stipulated by the Executive Yuan as the lowest limit. A slight difference leads to a great error, as the saying goes. Therefore, we must implore you to strictly correct them when reviewing the tax rates of the two provinces. Paying taxes is an obligation that the people should fulfill, but the level of tax rates is related to the national economy and the people's livelihood. The Committee has always admired your clear understanding and dares to present its humble opinions, respectfully requesting your adoption. We are fortunate and fortunate. We respectfully salute you."

▲Letter to Accountants Xulun and Yongzuo: "To Mr. Xulun Yongzuo, I have often heard that a country has its own special environment, and thus has its own special thoughts. It is impossible to transplant an entire academic theory to countries with different lifestyles. In terms of the current state of living, European and American countries have the highest production and the highest standards of living, while Japan has the highest production and a higher standard of living. China, on the other hand, has the lowest production, and the people cannot even achieve the lowest standard of living. This is evidenced by the increasing number of liquidations and the frequent bankruptcies when you and others perform accountant duties in Shanghai. The burden on the people is directly proportional to their production capacity and living conditions. If we must impose on the Chinese people the same amount of taxes that European, American, and Japanese people bear, wouldn't that be driving them to their deaths? Similarly, the public expenses for Chinese accountants handling cases cannot be compared with those of European and American accountants. This simple example is enough to prove it. We have heard that when Zhejiang province discussed business tax rates, a certain expert attended and said every day, 'This industry's tax rate is already low, and foreign countries should collect so much.' His intention seems to be that the Chinese business tax rates may as well follow the rates set by other countries, and there is no need to deliberate independently. Not only has he failed to give the slightest consideration to the declining state of Chinese industry and commerce and the exhaustion of the social economy, but he has also violated the Executive Yuan's guidelines on the business tax in various provinces. Does he have to see each industry go bankrupt and each store close down before he is happy? If you want to eat chicken eggs, you must cultivate the chicken itself. Killing the chicken for a momentary pleasure is not the economic policy that the country should adopt. Currently, Jiangsu's business tax rates are based on Zhejiang's rates, and the appeals of the sixty chambers of commerce in Jiangsu are indirectly due to the gift of a certain expert. The Shanghai business tax plan is currently being drafted and prepared by the Municipal Finance Bureau, and you are all members of the Finance Discussion Committee of the Municipal Finance Bureau. Since Jiangsu and Zhejiang have already erred in the past, this city must prevent it from repeating the same mistake. We are therefore offering this sincere advice and asking you to pay attention. A bone in the throat, it is good to spit it out. Offending words may be good medicine, and we hope you will take it to heart. We sincerely hope so. We wish you good health."

Meeting on Business Tax Rates 112

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce May Send Representatives to Attend

The Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Collection Outline and Implementation Rules have been passed by the Municipal Finance Discussion Committee. The issue of tax rates is still pending discussion at the third meeting. According to news from the Municipal Finance Bureau, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce may send representatives to attend the meeting.

Rice Merchants Discuss Business Tax Issues 113

The Rice Merchants Association of this city held an executive committee meeting yesterday afternoon, attended by more than a dozen people. Chairman Xu Jingzhi presided over the meeting to discuss the issue of business tax. The gist of the discussion was that since the central government promulgated the business tax, various provinces have formulated business tax regulations and are preparing to start collecting the tax. The tax rates in some provinces even exceed the central government's prescribed standard of two per thousand or twenty per thousand. Currently, various industries in this city are striving to negotiate, and a tax regulations research committee has been organized by various industries to specifically discuss this issue. However, the commodities of this industry must go through the procedures of traveling merchants, etc., before reaching the retailers. If a business tax of two per thousand has to be paid every time a traveling merchant is involved, the burden will inevitably increase sharply, and the price of rice will also inevitably rise, which will have a significant impact on the people's food supply. It has now been decided to hold another meeting to discuss the matter after the tax regulations research committee has made a definite statement.

Change of Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau 117

▲ Yuan Liang Resigns and Prepares for Handover

▲ Chen Xizeng is Selected as the Successor

Yuan Liang, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, recently received an order from the National Government to go to Japan to study police administration. Yuan Liang has submitted his resignation from the position of Director of the Public Security Bureau to the Municipal Government. The reporter from Nisshin Shimbun visited Yuan at the Public Security Bureau yesterday to inquire about the details of his resignation, the date of his departure to Japan, and the successor to the position of Director. Yuan provided a detailed answer. The conversation is recorded as follows: (Reporter's question) I recently heard that you have been ordered to go to Japan. Is this true? (Yuan's answer) I received an order from the National Government a few days ago to go to Japan to study police administration. Mayor Zhang also instructed me to study municipal administration. This is an order from the National Government, so I submitted my resignation from the position of Director of the Public Security Bureau to the Municipal Government yesterday. (Question) Has the date of departure to Japan been determined? (Answer) Since I took office as Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau on May 16, 1929, it has only been twenty months. However, because Shanghai is a corner where people from all directions gather, public security matters are of great importance, and I have been striving to do my best day and night, and I am fortunate to have made no mistakes. However, I feel that my energy has been deeply exhausted. I suffered from hemoptysis a month ago, which was slightly relieved after treatment. However, it suddenly recurred the day before yesterday. Therefore, after this resignation, I plan to rest for a month before deciding on my next move. I also plan to go to Beijing in the next few days to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and personally explain my intention. (Question) Have you heard anything about the successor? (Answer) I heard that Chen Xizeng, the current Director of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, will succeed to the position of Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. (Question) Are you ready to hand over? (Answer) I am now preparing to hand over. At this point, the reporter saw that Yuan had many visitors, so he excused himself and left. According to reports, Chen Xizeng, Director of the Telegraph Bureau, went to Beijing one day and returned to Shanghai yesterday morning.

Sun Baoqi Dies in Shanghai Residence 118

▲ Passed Away at 10:15 Last Night

▲ Twenty-One Children Attending

Former Prime Minister Sun Baoqi had been living in Shanghai since retiring. He suffered from a gastrointestinal disorder last winter, and after treatment by a Western doctor, it would sometimes improve and sometimes worsen. Two months ago, his condition suddenly worsened, and he also suffered from diarrhea. Treatment was ineffective, and he passed away at 10:15 last night, at the age of sixty-four.

▲ Treatment Process: Sun had a history of gastrointestinal disorders. In October of last year, he went to the Sino-Western Sanatorium Hospital on Bausch Road for treatment. The French doctor at the hospital said that there were parasites in his large intestine and that treatment would not be effective unless the parasites were killed. So he used medicine and acupuncture for treatment. Unexpectedly, he developed diarrhea due to the strong reaction of the medicine and acupuncture, which caused chills and fever from time to time. He then used quinine to reduce the fever. Because of his old age and weak physique, he could not support it. He was hospitalized for two months, and his vitality was greatly damaged. He had no choice but to move back to his residence on Jessfield Road, where he changed to Chinese medicine doctors Wang Zhongqi and Xia Yingyun for treatment. They both used ginseng and antler tonic products, but they were also ineffective after taking them. The diarrhea was the same as before. He also asked German doctor Polo and Dr. Huang Zhong to see him, but they all said that his original energy was too weak, and there was no significant effect. By 8:00 last night, he had reached the most dangerous time, and he passed away at 10:15 last night.

▲ Family Situation: Sun has six sons and sixteen daughters. The eldest son, Yongshi, is currently the manager of the Sumitomo Bank. The second son, Yongzhen, is the Deputy Consul of the German Consulate in Hamburg. The rest are all studying at school. The youngest son is only eight years old. Except for the second son, Yongzhen, they were all attending to him. After his death last night, his family immediately telegraphed relatives and friends in Tianjin and other places to announce the news.

▲ Sun's Brief Biography: Sun Baoqi, also known as Muh Han, was from Hang County, Zhejiang. He was sixty-four years old. His father, Yijing, was a Hanlin scholar in the Southern Study and served in the Yuqing Palace, teaching Emperor Dezong. He rose to the position of Vice Minister of the Ministry of Revenue. Sun was admitted to the officialdom through privilege and assigned to the Ministry of Punishment as a principal. In the twenty-first year of Guangxu, he was transferred by Wang Wenshao, Governor-General of Zhili, to the Beiyang Commission as a Daotai. In the twenty-fourth year, he was recommended as a talented official and summoned by imperial decree. In the twenty-sixth year, he went to Xi'an to handle official telegrams for the Military Affairs Department. Two years later, he was appointed as envoy to France. After completing his term, he returned to China and was appointed Governor of Shuntian Prefecture. The following year, he was ordered to be envoy to Germany. The following year, he was appointed Deputy Director of the Jinpu Railway.

Sun Baoqi's Portrait 119

After returning to China, he was released as Governor of Shandong. In the third year of Xuantong, the people's army launched an uprising in Wuhan, and he retired due to illness. In the Republic of China, he served as Minister of Foreign Affairs and concurrently as Acting Prime Minister. He was then transferred to the position of President of the Audit Court. In the fifth year, he was transferred to head the Ministry of Finance, and then transferred to the position of Director of the Customs Administration. In the twelfth year, he served as Prime Minister. During Duan Qirui's administration, he was appointed as ambassador to Russia but did not take office. In the fifteenth year, he retired from Beijing. In the seventeenth year, he went south and lived in Shanghai. He had great ambitions when he was young. During the Sino-Japanese War, most people in the capital advocated war, but he held dissenting views and almost suffered misfortune. Later, as an envoy, he repeatedly submitted memorials to request the establishment of a constitution and the reform of politics. Modern diplomats are either his subordinates or his disciples. When Cao Kun was in power, he served as Prime Minister. Because he opposed the Gold Franc case, he firmly refused to countersign it, which was praised by the times. He served as Director of the Customs Administration for seven years, and he always prioritized the interests of merchants and did not regard accumulation as a skill. After thirty years in office, his official bag was empty, but he was never stingy with charitable causes and helping friends and relatives in need. He always lent to them. He was clean and honest, and both Chinese and foreigners admired him.

Two Jiang Ships Have Accidents 121

The Yiping, a vessel of the Yiping American Jiejiang Company, was en route from Shanghai to Yichang this time. When it was about 140 Chinese miles from Hankou, the water level was very shallow. Six Yangtze River vessels had long stopped night navigation for fear of accidents. Unexpectedly, the Yiping sailed upstream this time, coinciding with a decrease in the water level. Local bandits, in order to rob passing merchant ships, secretly moved the navigation warning lights set up by the Customs in that area. The Yiping, unaware, mistakenly entered a shallow beach. The hull was stranded, but it managed to pull itself out. However, the bottom of the ship was damaged and could no longer sail upstream. It immediately unloaded its cargo and passengers and returned to Shanghai. After arriving in Shanghai yesterday, it has already entered the factory for repairs. The warning lights moved by the bandits have been moved back to their correct positions by the Xunhan Customs.

The Yuanjiang Maru, an upstream vessel of the Yuanjiang segment, of the Nisshin Company, travels the Yichang route. On the first of this month, the ship sailed from Hankou to Yichang. Seventy miles upstream of Hankou, in the Jiayu Tao area, the river water was sharply receding, and there were often moving reefs in that area. Since the communist disturbances, the setting of warning lights has often been lost. The Yuanjiang Maru actually hit a reef in Jiayu Tao. The bottom of the first cabin was breached, and river water rushed in. Since it was heavily loaded, the second cabin was also affected. The passengers were greatly alarmed, and the hull was in extreme danger, with a precipitous tendency to sink. Fortunately, the company's Dangyang Maru, en route from Hankou to Yichang, rushed to rescue after receiving the news. According to follow-up news obtained yesterday, the passengers of the Yuanjiang Maru have been transferred to the Dangyang vessel, and the cargo is completely submerged in water. The vessel has sunk into the river, five feet below the waterline. The situation is still extremely dangerous. If the water level rises by one foot, the Yuanjiang will sink and be lost. The Hankou branch of Nisshin Company has sent barges to rescue the ship and has requested Japanese warships to sail to protect it.

The manager is Wang Huailian, the assistant manager is Yan Dayou, and the brand name is added with the word "Yuan", becoming Jukang Yuanji Bank. (6) Xiangxiang Bank, also with changes in shareholders, with Zheng Zibin having six shares, Zheng Peizhi having three shares, Qin Heqing, Zheng Bingquan, and Feng Shouzhi having one share each, totaling twelve shares, with a capital of 300,000 taels. The brand name is added with the word "De", becoming Xiangxiang Deji Bank. (7) Tongchun Bank has hired Hu Ziheng and Wu Youxiang as assistant managers.

Shanghai-Ningbo Vessels Implement Increased Escort Teams 125

▲ Twenty-Two Constables per Vessel

▲ To Be Implemented on March 1

Shanghai-Ningbo vessels are discussing increasing the number of escort teams to prevent pirates, as previously reported in this newspaper. Now, this matter has been proposed by Sanbei and others, and the method has been drafted immediately. It has also been requested from the Songhu Garrison Command that constables be sent on board to serve as escort teams. It has been decided to implement it on March 1. The details of the method are as follows:

▲ Name: China Merchants, Ningbo-Shaoxing, etc., have publicly recommended Yu Qiaqing from the Sanbei Company to draft the charter system for the escort team in order to increase the number of escorts early. Yesterday, Yu, together with the two bureaus, agreed that the escort team should be named the Shipping Self-Defense Corps. A draft of forty-eight articles of association was specially drafted to regulate the duties of the corps members. In Shanghai, it was decided to set up an office of the Shipping Self-Defense Corps to manage all the affairs of the corps soldiers on the Xinjing, Tianning, Xingning, and Xinning-Shaoxing ships.

▲ Troop Strength: It has been agreed that the Shipping Self-Defense Corps will have one commander, who will be used by Xinjing, Tianning, Xingning, etc. There will be two deputy commanders with a monthly salary of 40 yuan each, two squad leaders with a monthly salary of 25 yuan each, and twenty-two soldiers with a monthly salary of 20 yuan each. The above is the number of officers and soldiers used by one ship. Each vessel will be equipped with 36 handguns and 24 wooden shell guns. In total, the three vessels will have six squad leaders, sixty-six soldiers, one hundred and eight handguns, and seventy-two wooden shell guns. The companies will receive them from the Garrison Command. The uniforms are in the drafting stage.

▲ Responsibilities: Yesterday, the three companies, having had a meeting, stipulated the responsibilities of the commander, squad leaders, and soldiers. The commander is responsible for training and guiding all squad leaders and soldiers, and has the power to promote, demote, reward, and reprimand. The soldiers' responsibilities are to be assigned to guard the interior and exterior hatches of each vessel to prevent pickpocketing. If there are suspicious people, they will jointly inspect them with the captain and the Water Public Security Bureau. If military equipment, etc., is found, it will be sent to the commander for forwarding to the company and the government. Soldiers will be stationed in the captain's office, the accounting room, the engine room, and the upper and lower hatches. In case of fog or rain, the squad leaders must go to high places to watch. Each vessel will also have three plainclothes soldiers as spies, and one female inspector will be added to prevent bandits, etc., from mixing into the vessel as women.

▲ Implementation Draft: The draft has been prepared, and it has been decided to request the Garrison Command to transfer sixty-six constables off the ships. All military uniforms, salaries, and food will be supplied by the shipping bureau. The draft will be implemented after it is revised. Therefore, requesting soldiers to board the ships is scheduled for March 1.

Heavy Fog at Songkou Yesterday 126

Forty River and Sea Vessels Unable to Enter Port

The fog in Shanghai yesterday was the worst in recent memory. All river and sea vessels of various companies were blocked outside Wusongkou, and no vessels arrived in Shanghai all day. This situation is the only in recent years. The reports are as follows:

▲ River and Sea Vessels All Blocked: Yesterday, the fog outside Wusongkou was even heavier than in Shanghai, and it did not disperse all day. Only the China Merchants' Xinjing and the Sanbei's Ningxing vessels, due to their regular Shanghai-Ningbo schedule, which could not be missed, ventured into the Huangpu River at 7:15 AM. They arrived at Wusongkou and anchored at 4:30 PM in the afternoon, waiting for the fog to clear before continuing. Other Yangtze River vessels of the Six Companies, such as Xinningxing, Anqing, and Wusong, were anchored at the mouth of the Yangtze River to avoid the fog. Some, scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the morning of the 2nd, have still not been able to arrive. Sanbei Company's new vessel, Sanbei, also had its propeller damaged. Yesterday, the Six Companies, seeing that no vessels had arrived, sent out wireless telegrams to inquire. They said that the sea was a vast expanse, and it was impossible to distinguish the waterways and incoming vessels, so they dared not travel. If the fog can disperse today, they can come, they said. Coastal vessels, such as Jardine Matheson's Shun Tien of the Northern Line, Ewo's Guisheng, Dalian's Dalianxiao, and Nanyang Line's Niuzhuang and Shandong, Great Britain's mail steamer Melville, and Italian mail steamer Venizelos, etc., were all blocked beyond Sanjia Shui. Three cargo vessels from the Pacific Ocean were also blocked and could not enter. Jardine Matheson's tugboats went to tow them several times, but they returned to Shanghai because they could not distinguish the routes. As a result, not a single river or sea vessel entered the port yesterday, a rare occurrence.

▲ Huangpu River Surface Guarded: After 5:00 PM yesterday, the surface of the Huangpu River was already misty, as if in smoke, and it was impossible to distinguish anything at a short distance. All of the companies' small ferry boats across the river stopped operating half an hour earlier. The civil boats and cargo barges in the river also docked early and stopped working. From 6:00, no ships were traveling on the river. The British and French warships on the surface of the Jingjiang River outside the sea, fearing that other ships might collide with them, implemented a guard. They rang a warning bell every minute and sounded a foghorn every three minutes. The sound of "woo-woo" and the ringing of bells all sounded together for a while. It was also heard that Changxing Company's Empress of Canada, originally scheduled to leave for Hong Kong on the 5th, was delayed to Shanghai by one day due to the fog, so it was rescheduled to leave the port on the 6th.

Postal Workers Demand Housing Allowance 128

▲ Representative Assembly Held Yesterday to Discuss

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union held a meeting the day before yesterday to discuss the issue of housing allowances, among other matters, and resolved to negotiate with the authorities. At 9:00 AM yesterday, the union dispatched representatives Zhang Kechang, Lu Jingshi, Zhu Xuefan, Qi Jiamou, Meng Shuxiu, and others, nine in total, to the General Post Office to submit a petition in person. At that time, the new Director-General, Qian Chunqi, was in Beijing and had not yet returned. Secretary Yang Sili came out to meet them, explaining that Director-General Qian had not yet returned and could only temporarily accept the petition for forwarding upon his return tomorrow (i.e., today). The representatives, having failed to achieve their objective, returned together. Yesterday afternoon, the union held a representative assembly to plan response strategies and discuss issues such as collective exemption from income tax and management of the fund. The Guowen News Agency reporter then met with Zhang Kechang, the executive member of the union, and the conversation was as follows:

▲ Zhang stated, in brief, that housing allowances were already in place in places like Beijing, Tianjin, Jinan, Harbin, and Nanjing. In Shanghai, only the Second Transportation Division had it, while other staff were still in the process. Today, we went directly to the bureau to request an audience with Director-General Qian, intending to submit a petition in person to him. To our surprise, Director-General Qian had gone to Beijing and had not yet returned, but he is expected to return tomorrow (i.e., today), at which point we will make the request again. Furthermore, the petition has already stated that a response must be given within ten days from today. Therefore, we expect a solution upon Director-General Qian's return to Shanghai. As for future action plans and strategies to be adopted in the event of necessity, these will all be determined at today's assembly.

▲ Main Points of the Petition Yesterday, the nine representatives of the union went to the General Post Office to submit a petition. The main points of the petition stated that, as the cost of living is rising daily, renting a house in the concessions costs several tens of dollars per month. While housing in remote areas is cheaper, the cost of transportation is also considerable. Employees who earn only a few tens of dollars a month are already struggling to afford housing alone. Therefore, we earnestly request that the authorities provide a monthly allowance of ten dollars to all levels of staff below postal officers. Furthermore, the housing allowance has been in place in the capital for many years. In other places like Pingjin, Ji, and Ha, in addition to housing allowances, there are also coal allowances. Therefore, Shanghai would not be the first to implement this. Even postal directors, who have relatively high salaries, have housing rents of over a hundred dollars paid for entirely by the bureau. Compared to employees who earn only a few tens of dollars a month, it is even more difficult to make ends meet.

Sino-American Joint Venture in Shipping 129

▲ Terms Not Yet Agreed Upon by Both Parties

▲ Li Zhonggong Has Gone to Beijing to Negotiate

It has been widely rumored recently that China and the United States will jointly operate Chinese shipping, which was initiated by Mr. Dollar, the owner of the American Dollar Steamship Company. During his last visit to Shanghai, Mr. Dollar proposed conditions to Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, which were that the ships would be provided by the Dollar Company, and the shipping operations would also be managed by them, but under the Chinese flag. The company would pay a certain percentage of the profits to the Chinese government, and the company would register with the Chinese authorities and be supervised by the Chinese Shipping Administration. The company's headquarters would be located in Shanghai, initially operating routes between Shanghai and Hankou, Shanghai and Ningbo, Shanghai and Fuzhou, and Shanghai and Tianjin, etc. After receiving the proposal, Foreign Minister Wang forwarded it to Minister of Communications Wang Boqun. Minister Wang expressed disagreement with several points and advocated operating based on the model of the China National Aviation Corporation. Minister Wang's response to Mr. Dollar was that the National Government's policy was to accept the management of all ships, utilizing American capital to develop Chinese shipping. The Dollar Company could lend money to China to develop shipping. The loan would be repaid over a period of fifteen years, and the National Government would control personnel and administration for shipping operations. In addition to inland and coastal routes, overseas routes should also be established, etc. The Dollar Company has not yet responded. Li Zhonggong, the Director-General of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, has now gone to Beijing to negotiate the matter. Last Sunday, when Minister Wang was in Shanghai, reporters also asked him about this matter. Minister Wang replied that China is currently negotiating the recovery of navigation rights. The purpose of the Sino-American joint operation of shipping is to prepare for the development of Chinese shipping after the recovery of navigation rights. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs and shipping experts are currently studying the matter.

Yesterday's News on Sino-German Aviation 130

▲ Trial Flight on March 1st, Inauguration in April

▲ Twice Weekly Round Trips, Carrying Passengers and Mail

Sino-German Aviation is now scheduled to conduct a trial flight from Beijing on March 1st. It is expected to officially launch in April. The Sino-German Aviation Corporation has purchased five six-seater Junkers aircraft. Two of these aircraft are en route from Germany to Shanghai and are expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 12th of this month. The fifteen pilots and navigators hired are all German nationals and are also expected to arrive in Shanghai soon. The current provisional plan is that, after the official launch, Shanghai will be the starting point, and the route will pass through Nanjing, Beijing, Shenyang, and Harbin, with the final destination being Manzhouli. There will be two round trips per week, carrying passengers and mail.

Henan Chairman Liu Sends Urgent Telegram Pleading for Disaster Relief 134

The Chinese Red Cross Society yesterday received a telegram from Liu Zhi, Chairman of the Henan Provincial Government, pleading for disaster relief. The plea was earnest and unbearable to hear. It is urgently disclosed as follows: "Received telegram from Zhang Fang, Director of the Henan Civil Affairs Department, from Luoyang, stating that he had met with various county magistrates along the way, who all reported a severe shortage of grain and funds, leading to a rise in banditry. He passed through Xin'an, Mianchi, and Xia County, where the poor were impoverished and without food, and even the rich were crying out in hunger and cold, a truly pitiful sight. The army has money but cannot buy rice. We earnestly request that you instruct the relief association to first implement price controls to alleviate the immediate crisis. If that is not immediately feasible, please negotiate with the Railway Bureau to prepare a train to transport grain, thereby rescuing the remnants of the people. We also request that you promptly send telegrams to the National Government and various charitable organizations to raise relief funds, so that dying disaster victims may receive assistance. We await your response with utmost anticipation." It has been investigated that Henan Province has suffered deeply from natural disasters and war. We have previously sent telegrams to various charitable organizations to solicit funds for assistance and also telegraphed the Central Government to request a disbursement of 100,000 yuan for direct disbursement of urgent relief in areas affected by the war. However, a cup of water is insufficient to extinguish a burning cart of firewood. As winter approaches, the cold and hunger are compounding the suffering. Fundraising in various places is limited, and it is difficult to implement price controls. The sight of misery everywhere is truly pitiable. In addition to telegraphing the Central Government to continue allocating relief funds, we also ask that you have compassion for the remnants of the people and solicit relief funds to be remitted continuously. We await your response with utmost anticipation." Liu Zhi, Chairman of the Henan Provincial Government.

Shaanxi Relief Delegation Arrives in Shanghai 135

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Society yesterday received the original letter from the relief delegation sent by the Shaanxi Branch, as follows: "Investigated the severe disaster situation in Shaanxi Province, the miserable conditions are evident. Winter and spring relief needs to be prepared early to save the remnants of the people. We hereby send Mr. Li Runzhi as a representative of our society to appeal to the Shanghai-Nanjing area, and we hope to provide guidance when the time comes." According to Mr. Li, although there was some planting in the province in the autumn, it was all damaged by insects, resulting in no harvest. More people are starving to death. Refugees in the countryside are not only demolishing houses and selling them as firewood, but also transporting farm tools and stone mills from hundreds of miles away to sell in the city. In this snowy and icy weather, without clothes or food and homeless, if rescue is not provided in time, another tragedy of starvation will occur. Not only is winter relief urgently needed, but spring relief must also be prepared early, as farm tools have been lost and seeds are lacking, making cultivation even more difficult. We hope that all parties will act with compassion and rescue these remaining people as soon as possible, so that the people of Qin will not all be buried in ditches, etc." It is heard that the society is also deeply anxious due to a shortage of funds.

▲ Fire Brigade Commissioners from the Public Works Department Inspect

French Concession Court Order Regarding the Day and Night Bank 146

The Order Has Been Delivered to the Day and Night Bank and the Great World

▲ All Assets Must Be Properly Safeguarded

▲ Chinese and Western Pharmacies to Operate as Usual

The French Concession Mixed Court heard the case of the Day and Night Bank the day before yesterday. The creditors applied for provisional attachment, which was approved by the French Court. However, the so-called provisional attachment is to ensure that all assets are properly safeguarded and not arbitrarily disposed of without authorization. Moreover, only the Day and Night Bank and the Great World Entertainment Center are subject to this attachment. The Chinese and Western pharmacies and the Jiu Fu Company are still operating as usual and are not affected. The French Court order is recorded as follows: The Shanghai French Concession Mixed Court issues this notice. The case is brought by creditors Xu Peiyuan and others regarding the debt owed by the Shanghai Day and Night Bank and the Great World Amusement Center. In order to preserve compulsory enforcement, an application has been made to the court for provisional attachment of all the debtor's assets, and the court has approved the application. It is hereby notified that the debtors, the Day and Night Bank and the Great World, shall immediately comply with the order to properly safeguard all assets and not arbitrarily dispose of them without authorization, so as to avoid legal penalties. (▲□) Absolutely do not disobey. This order is issued on February 3, 2020, by Gong Xiang, judge of the Shanghai French Concession Mixed Court. (Criminal Law of the Republic of China) ▲ Article 337: Whoever intends to illegally possess property belonging to another person for himself or for a third party is guilty of theft and shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than five years, detention, or a fine of not more than five hundred yuan. Attempted crime under this article shall be punished. □ Article 339: Property owned by oneself that has been sealed up or is liable for debt shall be treated as property belonging to another person in relation to crimes under this chapter.

The 630,000 Yuan Swindle Case Concludes 149

▲ The Civil Portion Has Also Been Judged

▲ The Property Is Under the Management of the Creditors' Group

▲ The Loan Receipts Will Be Returned as They Are Presented

Yang Shulin (courtesy name Yintang) from Tianjin previously opened the Hexing Wenji counterfeit silver company at the intersection of Xinzha Road and Changsha Road in the Public Concession, defrauding deposits of 630,000 yuan, fleeing and being arrested, and being escorted to the Shanghai Special District Local Court, where he was sentenced to twelve years in prison, etc. This was previously reported in the newspapers. It is now learned that the civil portion of the case, after the creditors' group hired lawyer Dong Yu to file a lawsuit, the court ordered the loan receipts of each creditor to be submitted for review. Therefore, registration procedures were handled at that time, and the loan receipts of the creditors were submitted to the court. The court has held several hearings, and it is now known that the case has been judged. All of Yang Shulin's property will be managed by the creditors' group. The loan receipts previously submitted have been returned as they are presented. Each creditor can bring the receipt to Dong Yu's law firm on the fifth floor of No. 9, Sichuan Road, Simalu (Fuzhou Road), to collect the funds. Russian Accused of Gambling and Embezzlement 150

The president of the Russian Military Society at 91 Route Tenant de la Tour, Gao Lai Si Re Gao Fu, and attorney Yan Qiu Fen Ling, have filed a lawsuit in the Special District Court against Shu Hai Ying Peng and Fan Che Lin, accusing them of gambling and embezzlement. They request legal punishment and an order for compensation for losses through civil suit. The defendants have retained attorney Wei Wen Han to file a defense and counterclaim. The case was heard in the third court by Judge Feng Shi De on January 26th. However, due to the absence of the first defendant, Ai Hai Ying Peng, the hearing was postponed to February 2nd. On February 2nd, the case was heard by Cheng Shang Feng, but Judge Cheng had many other cases, resulting in insufficient time. The hearing was then rescheduled for yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. The details of the hearing and the defendant's defense are recorded below:

▲ Gao Lai Si Re Gao Fu's Testimony

At 3:30 PM, after Cheng Shang Feng took his seat in court, he first questioned Gao, who described the embezzlement by the defendants and the operation of a gambling den at the Russian Military Society at 91 Route Tenant de la Tour. The testimony was generally the same as the previously published complaint, so details are omitted. After the testimony, the judge asked: "In February 1930, you sent a letter to Fan Ban Lin, stating that the club had no relationship with you. Is the signature at the end of the letter your own?" Gao replied, "It seems like it was my signature." The judge asked again to be sure, and Gao replied, "It was my signature." The judge asked, "Is your secretary Hua Gen Song?" Gao replied, "Yes." The judge asked, "On November 22, 1930, the first defendant, Ai Hai Ying Peng, sent you a letter. Is that correct?" (The original letter was presented to Gao for review). After reviewing the letter, Gao replied, "That's correct." The judge asked, "The first defendant's letter stated that the club's business was not good and that they were planning to close it down after January. Is that correct?" Gao replied, "Because we were planning to buy a portion of Bao Men's shares, that's why he wrote that letter." The judge asked, "But you wrote back to him, telling him not to resign. Did you write that letter yourself?" Gao replied, "I wrote the letter." The judge asked, "Did the defendants later write to you again, saying that they were definitely not going to continue? Was there such a letter?" Gao replied, "Yes, there was." The judge then summoned Gao's secretary, Hua Gen Song, for questioning. Hua testified that he was a 35-year-old Russian and worked as a clerk for the plaintiff. The judge said to Hua, "You must tell the truth about what you are asked in court. If you lie, you will be punished." Hua replied, "Yes." The judge asked, "Did you write the letter that the plaintiff sent back to the defendants?" Hua replied, "Yes." The judge asked, "Did the plaintiff sign his name himself?" Hua replied, "He signed it." At this point, the defendant's lawyer, Wei Wen Han, stood up and asked Judge Cheng to ask the plaintiff what he meant by the first article of the contract signed on July 24, 1929. Judge Cheng immediately asked the plaintiff, and the plaintiff replied, "The first article roughly states that Bao Men and Luo Men Si Ke Wei Qu each receive half."

▲ Ai Hai Ying Peng's Testimony

The judge asked, "What do you do for the plaintiff?" Ai replied, "I am the manager." The judge asked, "Do you have shares in the club?" Ai replied, "He is the president and manages the members' affairs. I am the manager and manage the club's affairs. I also have no shares." The judge asked, "Do you gamble and skim profits in the club every day?" Ai replied, "Our club is the same as other clubs. We read newspapers and sometimes gamble a little." The judge asked, "Does the plaintiff often write letters to you, telling you not to gamble?" Ai replied, "On October 22nd of last year, we sent a letter to the plaintiff, stating that we were quitting." The judge asked, "Did the plaintiff send letters to you, telling you not to gamble?" Ai replied, "Yes, he did." The judge asked, "Then how many letters were there in total?" Ai replied, "About one or two letters in December." The judge asked, "You filed a complaint against the plaintiff at the Zhabei Police Station. Why?" Ai replied, "He threatened me with a gun, so I reported it to the Zhabei Police Station." The judge asked, "When?" Ai replied, "December 30th." The judge asked, "Did you go with them?" Ai replied, "Yes, I went with them." The judge asked, "How much time elapsed between the plaintiff threatening you with a gun and you reporting it to the police station?" Ai replied, "I reported it the next day." The judge asked, "Is the gun found by the police station the same one that the plaintiff used to threaten you?" Ai replied, "Yes, it is." The judge did not believe him and asked to send someone to investigate. The judge asked, "Who is currently keeping the club's furniture?" Ai replied, "It is entrusted to a French store for safekeeping."

▲ Fan Che Lin's Testimony

The judge asked, "What do you do?" Fan replied, "Nothing." The judge asked, "Did you put any money into the club?" Fan replied, "No." The judge asked, "The plaintiff said you are the 'face' and Ai Hai Ying Peng is the 'insider,' is that correct?" Fan replied, "That's not correct." The judge asked, "Do you often go to the club?" Fan replied, "I haven't been there for four or five months." The judge asked, "Aren't you always going there to gamble?" Fan replied, "I used to go there often, but I haven't been there for the past four or five months." The judge asked, "Do you have a share in the current furniture?" Fan replied, "I don't have a share. I only acted as a guarantor on the contract, and I have no other relationship."

▲ Debate Scheduled for Today

Lawyer Wei stood up and said, "May I ask the court, can a final verdict be announced today? If a final verdict can be announced, the defendant is willing to withdraw the counterclaim. If the hearing is postponed, the counterclaim will not be withdrawn." Judge Cheng then announced that the debate would begin at 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 4th. Lawyer Wei immediately stated that the counterclaim would not be withdrawn.

▲ The Plaintiff's Sorrowful Words

At this point in the hearing, the plaintiff requested permission from the judge to present a statement. The judge granted permission. The plaintiff then said, "I was a high-ranking military officer before the Russian Revolution. Now I am living in your country as a stateless national. I can only request that the judges of your country conduct a fair trial." After making this statement, Judge Cheng said, "The theoretical aspects can be discussed during tomorrow's debate. There is not enough time now," and then adjourned the court.

▲ The Defendants' Defense

The defense statement argues that the accusations are fabricated and requests a legal defense and counterclaim. The first defendant leased No. 8 Tongfu Road as the Russian Naval Club. All the furniture and equipment belong to Min Yu Ge Le, who bought it from Luo Men Si Ke Wei Qu, who bought it from Bao Men. There are contracts to prove this, and the plaintiff is one of the witnesses and cannot deny this. The first defendant has not embezzled anything. Furthermore, Lawyer Qiu Fen Ling previously sent a letter on behalf of the plaintiff, requesting that he have the right of first refusal when Bao Men leaves the club. This alone proves that the plaintiff fabricated the facts and made false accusations. As for gambling, that place is a club and should have appropriate entertainment. However, there has never been any gambling. The so-called appropriate entertainment is all stated in the contract. The plaintiff's fabricated accusations are surprising. Furthermore, the house belongs to the Terry firm, and the lease has now expired. It has been leased to a French firm, Shi Lai, for a monthly rent of 660 taels for a term of one year. The second defendant is only the guarantor for the first defendant and has no connection to the club. Based on the above facts, the plaintiff has committed a crime under Article 180 of the Criminal Law and is therefore submitting a defense and counterclaim, respectfully requesting that the court conduct a trial and deliver a verdict according to the law to prevent false accusations. Submitted to the Shanghai Special District Court.

Tang Hui Xuan's Case Against Wife Dismissed 151

▲ Tang Also Submits a Request to Withdraw the Complaint

Tang Hui Xuan, an American economics PhD, accused his wife of adultery with Chen Gen Wei, causing a sensation in Shanghai. His wife, Zou Ai Zhen, retained law PhD Zheng Yu Xiu as her defense lawyer. The previous newspapers have reported this. The court found that Tang's procedures did not comply with the Criminal Procedure Law and transferred the entire case file to the prosecutor's office. The chief prosecutor, Liu Mao Chu (who holds a French law PhD), thoroughly examined it and found many flaws, which he refuted. The prosecutor's decision is thousands of words long and should be noted by society. Excerpts are provided below:

▲ Decision of Non-Prosecution

Defendant Zou Ai Zhen, female, 26 years old, from Shanghai. Defendant Chen Gen Wei, male, 29 years old, from Shanghai. The above defendants are involved in case No. 288 of the criminal code of the Republic of China, concerning offenses against marriage. After a thorough investigation, this court believes that a decision of non-prosecution should be made. The facts and reasons are stated as follows: "Facts" Tang Hui Xuan, also known as Tang Chong Ci and Shi An, accused his wife Zou Ai Zhen of adultery with Chen Gen Wei. Because the first instance declared them not guilty, he appealed to the collegial panel of this court. The second instance reversed the original judgment, rejected the plaintiff's complaint in the first instance, and notified the prosecutor to investigate according to Article 343 of the Criminal Law. Reviewing the original case file, the plaintiff stated that he returned to the country in the 16th year of the Republic of China and resided with the first defendant at his mother's house, and they had two children. He also stated, "My wife often goes out with Chen Gen Wei. She is now engaging in various improper behaviors, which my friends have noticed and urged me to return. So I came back on August 9th. My wife took me to the kiosk to live and did not share the bed with me. On the 10th, she told me that she did not want to live with me. On the 12th, I moved out. On August 13th, I went to my mother-in-law's house, and my wife had already left. I asked the nanny, Zhou A Mei, who Ai Zhen usually sleeps with. She replied that Master Chen and my young mistress are husband and wife. They sleep in the same bed every day and live in the back parlor upstairs. When I heard this, I immediately told the nanny that I am the mistress's husband. Later, when I asked the nanny about what she said, she refused to say anything. Later, on the 16th, I went to my mother-in-law's house and saw Ai Zhen and Chen Gen Wei sleeping in the same bed. I immediately reported to the third division of the first district and brought two police officers with me to arrest them. It was 5:00 AM. I went upstairs to take a look first and then called the police to go up and pull them out. They were still fast asleep. Three of us went in. One was a plainclothes officer, one was a driver, and one was a friend of mine whose surname is Xu. I don't know his name. He is a friend of a friend. He was introduced by a friend. I don't know where he lives. He refuses to say where he lives. He works at the Public Security Bureau but refuses to come to court," etc.

During the appeal, he also said that he returned to the country in the 16th year of the Republic of China and lived at No. 2 Qiyun Lane, Da Nan Men. After Zou Ai Zhen returned to the country, she first lived at No. 2 Qiyun Lane and then moved to No. 890 Route Père Robert. Last year, she moved to her current residence at No. 821 Zhonghua Road, her mother's house. He also stated that he returned in the 16th year and lived with Ai Zhen for two months. He went to Hubei. In August of last year, a friend named Chen Pi Lan told me. Another friend, Zhai Yi Zhi, also told me, but he has already gone to Guangxi. These two came to my mother-in-law's house to find me and learned of the various actions. Another friend, Hu Hai Gu, saw the two of them riding in a car together. A foreigner, Bian Luo, saw Zou Ai Zhen without her pants on in a small room in the photography studio. He also said that they had not lived together since August 6th of last year. After I returned to Shanghai from Hankou, she refused me and told me to move to a hotel. Two weeks later, I went to Guangdong. On August 9th of this year, I returned from Hong Kong, and she refused to let me come back. Later, I stayed at her mother's house for one night and slept alone in the kiosk," etc. During the investigation by this office, Tang Hui Xuan stated that he returned from the United States in the 16th year and lived with Ai Zhen. In February of the 17th year, he first went to Nanjing and then to Hubei. I went to Hankou, and Ai Zhen also went with me. She stayed for three months. She returned to Shanghai because the children were sick. I lived in Hankou for eight months. In August of the 18th year, I returned to Shanghai and found Chen Wei Gen living in the house. Ai Zhen forced me to live in a hotel for two weeks. He also stated that when I was in Hubei, a friend wrote to me, saying that the two of them went out together. When I returned, I personally saw them flirting with each other. I said at the time that I could not stand this situation. At 6:00 AM on August 16th, I hired a car on the road and took two police officers, a friend surnamed Xu whose name is unknown, and a driver whose name is unknown, and pushed the door open. I went upstairs to take a look first and then came down to take the police officer He Feng Lin up. A friend also went up, and one police officer stayed downstairs. The driver also went up, I think. I directed the police officer to go in and arrest them. I stood at the door. They lived in the kiosk. The police officer only pulled the two of them up, etc. The main points of the first defendant's defense are roughly as follows: Because the plaintiff had syphilis, they had signed a written agreement to live in separate rooms for two years. This time, when he came back, he brought many women's belongings. On the 12th, they started talking about divorce, but I refused, etc. Combining the testimony of the second defendant and the first defendant's younger sister and stepmother, Zou Yu Shi, the second defendant was in the back parlor upstairs, and the first defendant was in the front parlor upstairs. The first defendant, his oldest child, and his stepmother slept on floor mats, and the youngest child slept in the bed. The younger sister, Yue Zhen, also slept on another floor mat. The three plainclothes officers first grabbed the second defendant and then went to grab Yue Zhen. The plaintiff said at the top of the stairs that she was not the woman. The first defendant heard the noise and got up to see what was going on and was arrested instead of Yue Zhen, etc. "Reasons" Based on the above facts, the actions of the defendants were either heard by the plaintiff or witnessed by the plaintiff. Some belonged to old matters, and some belonged to new evidence. In general, there are three main points: (1) the relationship between the defendants was too intimate; (2) what was heard about the incident at the photography studio; and (3) what was witnessed on the morning of August 16th. To clarify the truth, let us examine each point separately. A. The relationship between the defendants on weekdays. The second defendant lost his father at the age of six and was adopted by the first defendant's stepmother, Zou Yu Shi, at the age of twelve. He lost his mother at the age of fourteen. He lived in the Zou family, married a wife for two years, and after his wife died, he lived with his stepmother for another four years for convenience. Their relationship is in fact like that of a mother and son, which the plaintiff must have known. Therefore, the fact that the defendants went out together should not have started in the 18th year of the Republic of China. If merely talking and laughing with each other, lighting her cigarettes, and eating her leftover porridge are considered signs of impropriety, then men and women in all families must maintain strict distance from each other. However, this may not be the format of families after the European War. Moreover, according to the testimony of the stepmother, Zou Yu Shi, what kind of improper behavior did the second defendant show? Although the second defendant's nephew, Chen Zhen Han, voluntarily came to this office to testify that his character was not good, when asked what his relationship was, he said, "He owes me money." Therefore, his words are not credible. According to the plaintiff, his friends Chen Pi Lan and Zhai Yi Zhi came to his mother-in-law's house to find him and learned of the various actions. However, according to common sense, if the person is not at home, ordinary friends would rarely sit inside and chat. Improper actions would also not be done in front of any close friends. Moreover, the plaintiff cannot point out the addresses of Chen and Zhai, so it is clear that they are not accurate. On this point, one cannot help but think that the plaintiff is overly sensitive. B. The incident on March 31st of the 18th year. This matter was presented to the plaintiff by Bian Luo, a Czech technician at the Queen's Photography Studio, in the law office of Shi Ying after the complaint was filed. The plaintiff said that he met him for the first time at 4:00 PM on September 27th. The three of them talked about eating at Da Zhonghua on Sichuan Road. However, the letter from Lawyer Shi to Bian Luo was written on September 29th, so the testimonies do not match. Leaving that aside, there are many brothels along the Bund, so there are many opportunities for secret meetings. Why would the defendants go to a photography studio where someone they know lives upstairs? Even prostitutes on the street know to be discreet, so why would they open the door wide? Moreover, the defendants and Bian Luo are both shareholders of the photography studio. When foreigners address each other, they usually distinguish whether they are Mrs. So-and-so or Mr. So-and-so. Why would the defendant not know what kind of relationship he had and mistakenly assume they were husband and wife? Therefore, the testimonies of the Englishman, Ge Bi Te, and the Russian, A Ke Xi Si, that Bian Luo and the second defendant had a dispute over the store's accounts are more credible. This part should be considered unreasonable. C. The incident on August 16th of the 19th year. This is the main point of this case. According to the plaintiff, he stayed at his mother-in-law's house for one night this time. He learned about it on August 13th from the nanny, Zhou A Mei. However, since he was able to stay at the Zou family's house, the servant would definitely know what kind of relationship he had with the owner. The servant and maid have been there for two months, so they would definitely know whether this house is the Zou residence or the Chen residence. For secret messages, even if the servant is foolish, they would not casually say anything to guests. This is one suspicious point. Examining the entire case file closely, the plaintiff stated that he first saw the defendants sleeping in the same bed and then went out to call the police. In the appeal and complaint, he stated that he went to the police directly. The testimonies differ slightly. This is the second suspicious point. The plaintiff went to arrest the adulterers, which is a very serious matter, yet someone whose name is unknown followed to watch. Moreover, a friend who knew his surname but not his name and knew he worked at the Public Security Bureau but refused to say where he lived helped them. None of them could be invited to testify. This is the third suspicious point. As evidenced by the words of the servant Zhou A Mei and the police officer who arrested them on that day, Zhou A Mei did not admit to telling him anything and even said that they did not have an affair (see the appeal transcript of November 11th of the 19th year). As for the police officer, He Feng Lin, in two court hearings, he testified that he did not lay a hand on them and said, "On this day, I was on duty and saw a car. Tang Hui Xuan came out and said to me that he was going to arrest people. Later, he reported to the district chief and went with him. When entering the Zou family's door, the Tang surname called me to stand at the foot of the stairs. The Tang surname grabbed the two defendants and told me to take them to the bureau. The Tang surname told me not to enter the room, fearing that it would startle the defendants. So I stood at the foot of the stairs and did not enter the room. The three people who came with the Tang surname went to arrest them." Therefore, the defendants' criminal behavior cannot be proven. Based on the above conclusions, the defendants did not commit any crime. While preparing the official decision, the plaintiff submitted a request to withdraw the complaint. In accordance with Articles 244, Paragraphs 1 and 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a decision of non-prosecution is made as above.

Shanghai Public Utilities Bureau Plans to Supply Pudong with Tap Water 152

▲ Lai Yi Ferry to Establish a Water Plant

▲ North Hu Tang to Open Artesian Well

The Pudong area of this city does not yet have tap water facilities. Residents have always drawn water from the Huangpu River for drinking, and the water flow is turbid and not hygienic. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, recognizing the urgent need for tap water among the people there, has drafted a plan for a municipal Pudong water plant. It has been learned that the municipal government has decided to establish it and has approved an initial allocation of 80,000 yuan for the purchase of land and the ordering of machinery. The Public Utilities Bureau is consulting with the Land Bureau to purchase private land near the Lai Yi Ferry, You Long Pier, and Tao Yuan Zhai in Pudong for construction. The North Hu Tang of Lai Yi Ferry previously had foul-smelling water, and the Public Utilities Bureau designed and drilled an artesian well there, designating the open space north of No. 105 Lai Yi Ferry as the well site. This location is close to the proposed water plant site, so it may not be necessary to build it. However, the construction of the water plant will take at least one year to complete. For temporary relief, it is still necessary to drill another artesian well. It is reported that this plan has also been approved by the municipal government and is currently being actively carried out.

Declining Exchange Rate for Silver 153

Recently, due to the extreme shortage of silver coins and copper coins on the market, the bulk price has been consistently increasing. Therefore, the exchange rate for silver dollars has gradually decreased. Yesterday morning, one silver dollar could still be exchanged for five double-horn silver coins (equivalent to ten horns) plus 150-160 cash coins. In the afternoon, it was only plus 120-130 cash coins. One silver dollar could be exchanged for 2,540-2,550 copper coins, which is 70-80 cash coins and 100 cash coins less than the exchange rate a week ago. It is said that in the coming week, the exchange rate may decline further, or silver coins may be exchanged for no change at all. The price of copper coins may fall below 2,500 cash coins or increase, which is still uncertain.

Record of the Interrogation of the Kidnappers in the Cai Fu Lin Case 155

Cai Fu Lin, a comprador of the British American Tobacco Company from Pudong, was kidnapped twice and ransomed for 30,000 yuan each time. His first kidnapping occurred on March 14th of the 18th year of the Republic of China. The chief inspector of the Criminal Investigation Department of the General Police Station, Lu Lian Kui, and inspectors Tang Jian, Feng Zhi Ming, Liu Zhao Nian, Zhang Shao Qing, etc., have successively arrested the kidnappers Zhang Jin Sheng, Chen Xiang Long, Jin Cang Shou, Qiang Hong Xiang (also known as Zhang Hong Xiang), Wang Dao Shi (also known as Wang Xiao Gen), Zhang Jin Chun, Shao Ren Mei, the woman Zhang Qian Shi (Zhang Jin Sheng's wife), Chen Wu Shi (also known as Da A Jie, Chen Xiang Long's wife), etc., a total of nine people. The detailed circumstances are recorded below:

Cai Fu Lin lived at No. 56 Hede Road, Shanghai West. At 8:00 AM on March 14th of the 18th year of the Republic of China, Cai took his private chartered car to the office. While passing the corner of Hart Road and Avenue Haig, several kidnappers suddenly blocked the road, claiming to be sent by the tobacco tax bureau and asking Cai to go to the bureau to talk. They tied Cai up and put him in car No. 6746, which was parked by the roadside, and drove him to Route de Say Zoong in the French Concession, hiding Cai at No. 7, Lane 79. After about eight days, they moved him to No. 91 Zhou Jia Zui Road. On April 20th, he was ransomed for 30,000 yuan. After this case occurred, the police conducted a thorough investigation. Recently, Chief Inspector Lu Lian Kui and others found that this case was initiated by Chen Wu Shi, the wife of Cai Fu Lin's colleague Chen Xiang Long. She knew Cai and knew that his family was somewhat well-off. She secretly met with the kidnappers at the Da Dong Hotel and planned to kidnap Cai. Zhang Jin Sheng and Zhang Hong Xiang were in charge of guarding the hostage. Chen Xiang Long, Chen Wu Shi, Zhang Jin Sheng, and Zhang Hong Xiang were arrested. It was later found that Zhang Qian Shi was the one who delivered food to Cai every day, so she was also arrested. Later, Wang Dao Shi, the driver of the kidnappers' car, and Zhang Jin Chun, who wrote the ransom letter, were arrested. According to Chen Wu Shi, Jin Cang Shou was also involved in the scheme. Jin had been sentenced to five years in prison by the court on January 23rd of the 19th year for robbing a prostitute of her jewelry. Inspector Lu went to the Western Prison and brought Jin in for questioning. It was then learned that the license plate of car No. 6746 used by the kidnappers was fake. The real license plate number was 16746. The car was borrowed by Shao Ren Mei, a driver at the Mitsui Bank, to the kidnappers. Shao was also arrested and handed over to the Special District Court. Repeated interrogations were conducted, but because spectators were prohibited, it was impossible to record the details. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ge Zhi Qin held a public hearing. The police lawyer, Wang Yao Tang, stated that the court had instructed the police to investigate the landlord of the kidnappers' hideout and summon the plaintiff's younger brother, Cai Yun Lin, to testify. According to the police investigation, the house on Route de Say Zoong is currently owned by the Xie Long Company. It is said that the house has changed hands several times since the plaintiff was kidnapped. The house on Zhou Jia Zui Road is owned by the Sincere Company, which also recently purchased it. Therefore, they knew nothing about it. Cai Yun Lin is ill today and cannot attend court. He had previously gone to the police station to identify the kidnappers. He said that the person who directly negotiated the ransom with him was not among them. Cai's prescription was then presented as evidence. Then, Cai Fu Lin was asked to testify. Judge Ge then summarized the previous testimonies of the defendants and asked them questions. The defendants also retained lawyers E Sen, Fan Gang, and Jiang Rong for their defense. Judge Ge then ordered the defendants to be returned to custody separately and adjourned the hearing to next Friday for the start of the debate.

Hua Shang Public Bus Ticket Seller Beaten and Injured 156

▲ Bodyguards Refuse to Purchase Tickets

Shi Kang Nian (from Ningbo, 25 years old), the No. 12 ticket seller of the No. 4075 bus on the No. 3 route of the Zhabei Hua Shang Public Bus Company, was at the Datong Road Sun Temple station at 4:20 PM the day before yesterday when three bodyguards from the Zhenru District Second Regiment, members No. 103 Zhang Fu Quan, No. 114 Wang Jin Tao, and No. 129 Zhang Yi Bao, boarded the bus and refused to purchase tickets, leading to an argument. The bus stopped, and the three members jumped off the bus, grabbed the ticket seller Shi Kang Nian, and beat him severely.

Page 16

They struck him on the head, causing a hole and covering his face with blood. His waist was also severely injured. Kang Nian, unable to bear the pain, cried for help. The police officers from the Sun Temple police station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau came out and took the three assailants and the injured Shi Kang Nian to the station and transferred them to the Fourth District for processing. After questioning, they ordered Shi Kang Nian to seek medical treatment on his own. The three members were detained, but they were soon released on bail. After receiving a report from Shi Kang Nian, the bus company sent a letter to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau yesterday, requesting that the three assailants compensate for the losses.

Three Who Fell to Their Deaths 157

▲ Yu Shanzhong, a resident of Hua Ji Road, Donggui Fang, in a flat house, was from Yangzhou. He was over fifty years old and had long been a foreman at the docks. He had been in Shanghai for several decades and had many friends. He originally planned to return to his hometown tonight and come back to Shanghai in the middle of next month. Unexpectedly, some of his friends heard about this and hosted a farewell banquet for him last night. Yu couldn't refuse the gesture, so he went. After the meal, he was invited by another friend to see a Yangzhou opera at the Sanmin Theater on Xi'an Road. Being old and frail, while walking up the escalator on the middle level, he carelessly slipped and fell. His skull was fractured, and he bled profusely. He was taken to the Tongren Hospital for treatment by his friends, but his injuries were too severe, and he died yesterday afternoon.

▲ Li Maozhi was from Zhenjiang and was already in his seventies, living a solitary life. He currently resided at the Tongxinggong Inn in the Maijiaquan area of Shandong Road. He had previously opened the Chunyang Apartment in Xinkai River, but it closed due to poor business. Li had been idle for too long, was destitute, and could barely afford food and clothing. He was mentally unstable. At 11 a.m. the day before yesterday, he went to the Tianlaifu Electric Material Company on Simalu (Fourth Road) and Zhejiang Road to visit a friend. As soon as he went up to the third floor, he lost his footing and fell to the ground. The back of his head cracked open, and he was on the verge of death. Someone then called the police, and he was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Because of his age and weakness, the medicine was ineffective, and he died at 12:30 p.m. yesterday.

▲ Xu Er'er was from Wuxi and was 31 years old. He made a living selling fruit and lived at No. 309 Xiaoshadu Road in western Shanghai. His wife, Tang, was 30 years old. Last night, during dinner, he drank too much alcohol and became drunk, unable to control himself. At around 9 p.m., he insisted on inviting his neighbors to play mahjong. Unexpectedly, the light bulb had been borrowed by a neighbor. Xu disregarded everything and staggered over to ask for it back. The neighbor's wife said, "You can just take it off yourself." Xu immediately stood on a stool and climbed up. Carelessly, he fell to the ground, immediately lost consciousness, and was taken to police station No. 2893, then to Baolong Hospital. Because he had been in a coma for too long, he eventually died.

Innovation in Travel Magazines 158

▲ The January and February issues have been published

The Travel Magazine, published by the China Travel Service at No. 114 Sichuan Road, Shanghai, has been in publication for five years. It has been praised by the world for its exquisite pictures and text. The magazine should have a fixed date of publication. Therefore, starting this year, the magazine has signed a contract with the printing house to ensure that each monthly magazine is published at the beginning of the month, without the bad habit of being late. Therefore, the first issue of this year has already been published, and the second issue began to be sold yesterday. As for the content, starting from the first issue, it publishes the long novel "Like Fleeting Time" by contemporary famous novelist Zhang Henshui. The story is beautiful and can be called a masterpiece. In addition, the excellent works in the second issue include "A Month in Japan" by Cai Mohuai, "A Lifetime of Knowing the Taste of the Jianghu" by Zhao Shuyong, "The Scenery on the Ninghang Highway" by Cheng Jichun, "A Record of Exploring Plum Blossoms in Chaoshan" by Li Enxu, "A Guide to Luzhou" by Bo Shi, "A Travelogue of Jiuri Mountain" by Zheng Tingyu, "A Travelogue of Fengdu Twenty Years Ago" by Liu Puquan, "An Expedition to the South Pole" by Cheng Zhizheng, "Magazines of the Straits Settlements" by Kong Boyi, "A Guide to Europe" by Qin Lizhai, as well as "Travel Notes," "Traffic Snippets," etc. The works are like a forest, and they are beautiful and cannot be fully appreciated. The cover is still a three-color lithograph of beautiful scenery, and the size is slightly larger than before. The paper is still cream-colored coated paper. Each issue retails for 30 cents, a half-year subscription is 1.80 yuan, plus 18 cents for postage, and a full-year subscription is 3 yuan, plus 36 cents for postage.
